O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear sons, I have completed this book which is the last of the medical art with its contents and I have finished it by way of its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this treatise with you, which is part of the work by hand, that is to say, "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And for this reason the work by hand is well-treated in our region and is completely different from all others, so it has the science and the knowledge, and there is nothing left to be desired from the force of the hands but the small descriptions in books of the ancient ones that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come the error and the vanity, and the intentions are closed and the science is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	Or me seems that I will come to life again with the direction of this healer according to the way of exposure and statement and abbreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and I will come together with the forms of the tools of cauterization, and of the other instruments of the work with the setting of the statement and preparation for him, as it is fit.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because there are no good masters of hands found in our time, the art of medicine is extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who engages in this should master the science of anatomy, as Galileo says, to such an extent that he knows the judgment of limbs, and their shapes and connections and separations of bones, and has knowledge of nerves and veins and the number of joints, and movement and resting veins, and the place of their exit.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And for this do I say that he will not be bitter with the food, and little by little with the work;
et meismement en l’art de main.	and especially in the art of the hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We will say to you in the introit of this book that he who is not aware of the things before said, let him guard so that he does not err and hurt men;
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	So that I have often desired many of those who meddle in this science, and if they abandon themselves to this science and to their experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I have seen a foolish man who cut an abscess on the scrofulous neck of a woman, and he cut the arteries at the base of the neck.
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	because so much blood came out that the woman died between his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I have seen another foolish man who treated a stone in the bladder of an old man, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	so he took away a piece of the bladder with him, and the man died three days later.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already seen a patient called for an operation, and saw the dislocation of the patient and the size of the stone; and if one operated on him, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I have seen another foolish man who took as his cure a duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the break there was an ulcer;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the foolish physician, out of ignorance, tightened the break on top of the ulcer with a very tight bandage, and left no salve on the wound, leaving it in this condition;
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and he ordered that he not remove it.
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and causes delays so that the leg is all hidden and the foot and comes to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come to remove the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I removed it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But all the ways in which he had corrupted that limb were already confirmed, and that member could not be healed;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and the corruption did not cease to spread through the limb until all the members were lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another wonder that would cause an abscess to become putrid and then inflame because of the evil of its nature.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For leprosy, when it is infected with melancholy humor, does not come to touch it except with iron in such a way that all that is corrupted can be removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And therefore, dear children, you must know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is to say, there are those in which there is danger in many situations.
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show in each of the books of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For you must keep them so that the bad man cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you take your weapons in harmony, and tackle your patients lightly but resolutely, and employ the better method, so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and are healed;
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave behind the incurable diseases of great illness;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and keep your weapons from those who make you doubt, and believe that you may come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galien wrote some of his advice:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not take on a patient with a bad disease, lest you be called a foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	» I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters are about fire cauterizations and water-based medicines, and the chapter order from the loins down to the feet;
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and of the shapes of tools, and of the iron instruments for cauterizing, and of all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter deals with the use of knives for cutting, suction cups for sucking, and vacuum for extracting matter from wounds, as well as the extraction of arrows and similar procedures.
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and this is the order of the chapters and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter deals with the restoration of dislocations and torsions, and similar procedures.
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and here are the forms of instruments from the beginning to the end.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus we remember the work; it is necessary that I speak about the quality of aid and the harm of each color.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of aid, and its harm, are the most distant word and subtle science and secret responses.
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and from these words many wise men will speak, and agree with them.
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	And I am satisfied with few words, because I shorten the long.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that universal aid, in all parts where there is matter, except in two complexions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	This is hot in nature, and dry by substance.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In hot and dry complexions together with substance, there is no one who does not say that cautery is a great help;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and the other said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that cautery is of no value to a disease that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the fire nature is hot, and must not be cured of a hot disease by heat, nor by dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and he who says that cautery does great help to a hot and dry disease that comes about in men's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And all the ways, except those who have tried it and know by long use the treatment of fire, and the diversity of human complexions, and their dispositions and causes of diseases, and the wonders and space of time;
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	Of other complexions we have no fear, but of the cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all of them agree and are in harmony with the fire cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, sons, that fire cautery is more effective if it is applied to wounds that have already been treated, and it has much greater beneficial power than cauterization with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and comes only to the member that is wounded, and does not harm another member at all.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	The burning medicines come from one member to another by removing them, and bring to the member painful diseases of great repair.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and by chance the disease occurs.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fire for its height and because of the goodness of its substance does not cause it, if there is no surplus.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And which I have found by experience and by the length of service and study that I have put into this art, and is based on the wisdom of things;
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	And because I am sorry for the length of speech, for it does not please me to rob you of the secret which is hidden in fire, and the quality of the work, how he routs diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in his demonstration;
or le recevez en vos pensees.	and may you take it to heart.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they should be performed at the right time, and they should be prayed over.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cauterization is appropriate at all times, because the harm caused by what comes after can be prevented by cauterizing.
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and most often it is done for necessary and urgent pains that cannot wait until the time when greater and faster harm might come to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And do not think, young man, as they do,
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	because there is no returning from the disease that is healed by cauterization.
et il le dient ensi;	and it should be served in this way;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not the same as what they do; for cauterization is not like medicine that changes the appearance and dries up the humors that cause pain, nor does it have as quickly as medicine does, its power over its work and its dignity in its action.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And things that can be known are that the disease will never return according to the appearance of the patient and the location of the disease and its virtue;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and are gathered together in him the excesses by the acquisition of meat and similar things, if it is not that cauterizes are administered into him where he has a little excess and moisture, so as to cauterize with thick for the pain, and similar things, and the part pain does not return again;
mais ce avient poc.	but this did not happen.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand because the cauterizes of medicine are called the derrians, and it is seen;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cauterizes are good after medicine, but their intentions are wrong, and the cauterizes of the derrians of medicine are good because when we administered ways of treatment in any disease and they did not work, then let us administer the cautery, and it is good.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is clear that cauterizing the derries is useful for whatever reason when we administer ways to treat various diseases and they do not work, so let us administer the cautery, and it will be useful; but it is not according to the intentions of the foolish people.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancient ones said that the cautery of gold instruments is gentler than that of iron, and they did not say about the quality of gold and because of the high quality of its substance;
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the fire cautery does not cause ulceration, but that is not true because I have tested it, and I found that it is true in some people;
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and gold cauterizations are better than iron, as they used to say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And whenever you heat a gold instrument, it is not the same as when it is coated with gold, and it quickly cools down;
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if you heat it too much;
si font au feu;	so it does in the fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and so there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And so we use our fire cautery which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	For in this chapter on the head of the shoulder, order it so that the view is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	The olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	For this cautery with olive oil is for the head, and by reason of moisture and coldness on the head, and because of many humors that descend from the hair, and to the ears, and for many troubles and pain in the teeth and in the jaw, and most importantly for all diseases that come from coldness such as paralysis and sodomy and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged with a liquid medicine that softens the head (III or IV), according to what is appropriate for the virtue and the age and the habitude of the disease;
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then make a hole in the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then take the fire and sit it between your hands, and put your hands on his back.
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	After that, place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and then let your two fingers come together, and if it bleeds from the middle, heat the fire which is called 'olivaire', by which this form is made:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And place it on the mark of ink, and do it descending and drawing your hand back and forth again;
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	and then release your hand, and look at the bone I sole little;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	And if you don't see it, begin again the fire as long as you see the bone, as I told you;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	After that, take a little thread, and put it wet and soft cotton inside, and place it on the mark, and leave it for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	After me take cotton wet with butter.
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and leave on until the heat is gone;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	After me treat the wound with an ointment called "tetrafarmacon" until it is healthy again.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And say to him who is old, that the longer the wound remains open, the more it will fester;
et por ce si aide mues.	and for this reason one must act quickly.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they said that one must leave the fire cautery in place for so long that part of the bone is burned; and then remove what is burned from the bone, and it will heal.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And serve the other that he must be cauterized as long as it can be, and press so hard that the humor can come out of the bone as far as the women put in their thorns to get rid of the humor;
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one must leave the wound open for a long time;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	After this, you must treat and support it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two ways of cauterizing do not seem good to me in any way, except that in some people who are prone to fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and it seems to me that I must leave him alone.
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	because the shoulder is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we witness in other members;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and even when the shoulder of the sick person is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization is more calm and quiet for me, and from this I operate in a orderly way to save.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old woman's pain at the top
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When all the head comes to great pain and lasts a long time, then the patient must use his herbs and pills which are called "coches", and head washing and oils and plasters;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if on him the cauterization that we have just said is done, and it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take care if the shoulder of the sick person is of strong nature, and he is not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	then cauterize him a little as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After making fire cautery on each horn of the head just up to the bone, as we have said before, and make fire cautery where it is called "vessel";
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and put vials there;
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and arrange your hand so that you do not see the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patient feels too much pain in this fire cautery than in others, and I will speak about it later;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and the fire cauteries of the horns should be thinner than those for which you make fire cautery on the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	Dou cautere dou chief
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When sudden pain comes in part of the head up to the oil, and the patient is extended until the bone, and the shoulder has been cleansed with medicines that make one well, and all this does not help:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	then do fire cautery according to two ways, that is to say, of water medicine and of fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	To treat a medicine ague, if you squeeze an almond and scratch the skin but do not remove the flesh from the two shoulders, then make a temple where the pain is in some way that you can respond to the almond being removed from the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it has been responded to if the bandage and restraint are well done and left thus for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	then remove the bandage and treat with garlic, and leave the wound thus for two or three days;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then put cotton dipped in butter on it as long as it can stand it.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the garlic treatment until it is well;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you see that fire of some burning medicines that I have written or one-twelfth treatment of burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery if it is according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery so that it is this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And is called "close" for this head is made in the form of a close or it has a small crook, and is middle to a small appearance;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and set over the painful part, and hold your hand and turn the fire a little lighter, until half of the meat is burned.
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and leave your hand so that the artery does not burn, which will stop bleeding, and run with a great deal of blood.

de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat a headache as we have said before in the division of diseases, and do not profit from it, and see that the cautery which is called "cultellare" is blunted, then it is necessary to sharpen the cautery until it is white.

et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and so with caution from the mandible that moves when it is bitten, and the root does not hurt except for the movement and spasms that come to the patient, and so with caution from the blood loss of the artery when it is cut, or if there is a great fear and uncertainty in those who do not know about this, and who are not students and have not experienced it;

de la cure de fistule par cautere	For the treatment of fistulas by cauterization:
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When treating fistulas as we have explained in the section on diseases, and your treatments do not help, then you must apply cauterization according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Tell the patient to place his hand in your lap.
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and hold the hair of the patient's head between your hands so that it does not move or fall;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	after you have dipped a cotton swab in wine or juice of pomegranate on oil;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	after heating the iron instrument which is sharp;
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and place it on the head like the shape of a feather from a dove, together with the mouth so that the iron tool is:
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you see, if it is pointed at one end to the other, and if you do not see, if it is like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but anyway, this who is the head worth must move for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After press the fistula if it is open, and do a treatment of perspiration, and dry it;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if it is closed, if you work, and treat firmly the bowels;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	after put on the fire carefully, and hold your hand to the fire at the part down of the oil, that your hands do not make madness;
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and put the fire in the oil fat, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery just to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, if you restart the fire again once, and other than that you need to do, and leave it III days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	after I put on cotton wet in butter, and the care of the infection drying as long as it is healthy, and pass XL days that it is healthy, then put on medicine sour corrosive as long as the bone is uncovered;
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and let him choose according to what he will come with his chest.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And I know one way to cauterize a fistula, which no one of the ancients spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Listen to a fistula, and seal it up.
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	After that, we will place a thin layer of substance on the incision to protect it:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and we will make the quantity of one tablespoonful of paste;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold it firmly with your hand, and do not move the patient so that the melted paste does not run down to his oil;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is necessary that we put on the patient's cotton cloth wet with oil of olibanum or with ointment;
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	The paste should be applied to the hole of the fistula, and it will heal by a wonderful healing power.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the fire that we have spoken about, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then you should administer a punch to the nose, and bring back the fistula to the root of the nose according to what is suitable in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	in the fissures of the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	These times have caused fissures in the lips, which are called "warts", and most often in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these fissures as we have said in the divisions, and the cure does not benefit, then in a small cauldron according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And put it carefully in those crevices until it hardens;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, treat the hole with ointment until it is well.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When abscesses form in the root of the tongue or in the uvula, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after putrefaction and rot and are enveloped and become fistulas;
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you cure it as we have said in the divisions, and it does not benefit:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	then it is necessary that you have the cautery according to the quantity of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	after the opening or hole of the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron comes to the source thereof, and where it is;
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do so once or twice, after the cure we have said, until he is well;
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if it is cured so, it is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if not, it is necessary to discover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines, but that does not help, then put the head of the sick in your healthy one.
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	After warm the cautery so its form will come out after in a way that you put a chain over the teeth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and put inside it carefully, and hold it so that the sick person feels the heat coming from the root of the teeth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	After remove your hand and start again the cautery according to your will;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	After fill the sick person's mouth with salt water, and leave it for an hour and rinse it well.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	In this way the tooth which was moving is fixed, and the gums which were softened are tightened, and the moisture which corrupted is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain in the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When the pain of the teeth comes from cold, or there is cold or fever, and medicines do not help, then it is necessary to cauterize according to two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and fire cautery and butter cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	A cauterization with butter if it is such that you squeeze butter from a cow's udder, and the tip in a spoon of iron or brass.
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	After, take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a needle, and squeeze out the milk into butter, and put it on the sore tooth carefully and keep it in place until it cools down;
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and often so that its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if the wool and cotton become wet with butter and are put on the sore tooth, and put on iron hot until the fire comes to the root of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The fire cauterization together if it is such that you squeeze a piece of iron or brass wire, and make it thick so that the fire does not come to the mouth of the sick person;
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After, heat the cauterizer, so that its shape comes out later, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cauterization cools down;
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Make this frequently, for the pain will increase on the next day or the day after.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter when applying this fire cautery, and then quickly rinse it out.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	This is how you make the fire cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make this cautery on the corner of the mouth that you want to, and according to what you are able;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	This is how you make the cane:
des scrophules	of the scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When the abscesses are swollen and cold, and do not respond to medicines by means of digestion, then heat this head-cauterizer; for there are two openings so that the fumes can rise from one side and come out from the other.
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	And place the fire cautery hot on the abscess once, or where it is necessary to do so, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if it boils up, make a small cautery according to the quantity of the boil, and leave it like this for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and put cotton wetted with balm on it until the burn has healed;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, use oil and poultices until it is healthy again.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the leg:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When the moisture conquers the chest of the patient and most importantly when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient must be emptied first by soluable medicines;
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	Afterwards, make a cauterization at the root of the throat, and be careful not to go any further up the throat, and only apply it with a little heat.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	Afterwards, make another cauterization at the joint of the neck to the base of the spine, and let this cautery that is called 'clavicle' give us the shape beforehand;
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the wound as we have said above until it is healthy.
de la toust	of the toast
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all and the disease of the liver are cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or chills, and is an ancient disease, then make a fire cauterization on the lever in its eyes;
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and another cautery boils the urine between the breasts;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and let the cauterization which is called "the clavicle" according to the shape that has been said above.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see, make cauterization by poking at all the cauterization which is called "the point" of where the shape is above in the disease of the ears;
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and let the points only up to XXX, or stop before the end.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treatment, follow this method described earlier, and let the cauterization be done in three steps according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for those who are less able, do three together.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	to prevent the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	After, have the patient lie on his back and on his side;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	After, give the patient the potion that is inside the phlegm with both hands of your left hand;
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated from within, then heat the fire cautery that has two sides here is the form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize it until he pierces it up to the coast, and come the figure of the cautery all together four cauteries;
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and because it is made with fire cautery that has three sides, so that the form of cauterization are five cauteries;
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and they are the nerves according to the subtility of a thread and this is the form of the cautery that has three sides:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And never is placed on this nerve for there are 8 cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	After he puts himself on the fire cautery to grind with silk;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Then rest the patient, and do not move the limbs for a long time until they are well relaxed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated from above, such a thing happened, then make the cautery on the thick part of the cautery with a claw, or many cauteries pierce it.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joints are closed, and the moisture is taken from the bone, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach come colds and moisture as it is taken out of its composition, and are multiplied to him, and the customs of cures are used, and he does not benefit, then the patient should be carried on his back, and his legs and hands spread out.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	Therefore later he does three cauterizations one on the tip of the finger per the quantity of a grain, at all the cauterizes are crossed, and two cauterize from the two sides as much as the form of the cauterizes is made by three angles, and there is a part between each one that they do not join together when they move by fire;
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and let the cauterize be so perfect that it burns the two parts of the wound, and let the shape of the cauterys follow this form without touching:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you burn the stomach with a large cauldron according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and whoever has fear of this cauldron, burn and sign on the stomach at a point according to the quantity that you see fit to;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then let him burn all the cauldron which is called 'the point'.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the wound that we have had before, until he is healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	As for the liver, it comes pain from cold and moisture and thick windiness, as much as it is strongly removed from its natural composition by the excesses;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is cured of what we have said in the divisions, and it does not benefit him, if the patient is silent on his hemorrhoids;
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and mark with three caustics according to this form and this figure and this quantity on the liver, so that the hypocondes, from where the cuts of the ome come;
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and let there be space between each cautery the thickness of two fingers.
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and let the cautery be long all the way down, and do not press too much with your hand on all the cautery;
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	and be burned only halfway down, and let the patient lie on his back;
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if he cannot, then let him lie on his side, and extend his legs, and raise his breasts;
et c’est li forme:	this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if your will is, when you cauterize these cauterys of the skin, that you be subtle and wise in this art, and guard yourself so as not to burn all the way down, for you would parch the whole body;
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and let it not go any further than a pimple, for the cut is very delicate in that place, and the sight to see it.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	If he has an abscess in the liver, and you need to know whether it is in the parenchyma of the liver or in the capsule:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	If it's in the parenchyma, then the patient feels pain that isn't too intense;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	If it's in the capsule, then the patient feels acute pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And when this treatment for the blisters was finished, the patient would become confused about his head;
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then sign to where the abscess is and then heat the fire which is similar to a toothpick, so as to form it;
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize until the wound has all burned, and bring it down to where the hair grows, so that the scalp is completely furred over;
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the treatment according to the treatment of the ulcers until he is healthy;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	and it is not good for anyone who has not studied medicine to use this fire treatment, because these diseases have never been cured by it.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	And then he can take it as hard as possible, and it seems to me that he should leave it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	For the plagues,
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancient ones said that one must do for pleurisy root cauterizes of arisology, and by this method:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take a root of arisology that is long, the largest you can find, and dry it as well as making it as big and as long as your two hands.
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	and soak it in oil and hold it to the fire, and cauterize I cautery between the jaw and the neck, and two small cauteries one little descending into the part that is hairless;
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	and two cauterys between the fifth rib and the sixth, in going down a little behind;
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	and one cautery over the anus and another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two ribs farther back from the one that is between the shoulders;
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	and do not squeeze my hand, but make it open as well as you would when smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And said no old man that any man use fire cautery like a razor, and blow it and put it between the ribs, until he comes to the abscess.
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	and saunter for the pain, as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear or the patient dies now, or a fistula comes out which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have said in the division of treatments, and it does not benefit, then they devoted three ways of cauterizing that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant;	Of which there is a way that you do three cauterizations, or four, lining according to the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the fire cautery of the liver that we have said before;
et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	and do not press your hand on all the cautery, and let the patient be sore on his back;
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule;	and another way of cauterizing is that you heat the cautery that has two edges, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder;
et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	and leave the cut that is on the mouse's side, where the patient's cut comes towards the left, and let the elevations that you cut be aligned with the cut, according to the length of the body, and the cautery be aligned with the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII.	After, pour the two waters boiling as long as the sound of the knock is perceived from the other side, and then treat with fire, and so in it will be four.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	And if you see, then cauterize until all the cautery is three.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure has been left to stand for a long time, and this is true that the other cure in front of it must be finished.
de ydropisie	of droopsie
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Do not cauterize by the method called "ascultation".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis;	When you cure according to the ways we have said in divisions, and your cure does not benefit, then it is appropriate that you make four cauteries around the bouge, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the back of the spine, and one place on the pelvis;
et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	and let the cauterization be well placed near the cure.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere;	After, leave the fire open for a long time, and do not let the patient's wound remain untreated after the cauterization;
et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	And the healing would hurry, and both intentions would be together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit;	The shape of the fire cautery for the abdomen is like a nail that we have before us.
et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	and this for the back is olive-shaped, according to what it is described here in front.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the joints
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire;	When the feet are swollen in those who are hydropic and are pale yellow in color, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the index and the ring finger;
et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	and hold your hand with the cautery without turning back.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too far in all of it, lest the yellow [color] would be forced out, and the cautery is made according to its form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire;	After that, do two cauterization on each leg at the tip of the heel;
et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe;	and be the cautery long, one from behind the knee in front and the other away, in front of the leg;
et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse;	and leave the cautery on top for a long time without cauterizing, so that the blood comes out;
aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After this cure of those other cures that we have said.
de la menoison	of the mansion
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures;	When the solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, as long as the virtue that retenues and digests which is in the stomach and in the intestines is affloated, and cannot be cured by any way of cure;
et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule;	and you see the patient very suffering and of great virtue, so do I great cautery on the stomach according to what it has spoken before or cautery of the stomach, at the circulation of cautery;
et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	and four cauteries around the navel subtly to all cautery nail-like, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see moisture abundant and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the knuckle, and a cautery on each finger, and two small cauteries on the stomach, for the cure is profitable when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	in the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres:	When the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, or one or more, and are old and are great cold and moist corrupt humors, and are cured as we have said in the divisions, and does not benefit, if do cauteries:
III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois;	and three on the spine of the back, which is all out of the body slightly and slightly in squaring, and two cauteries around the navel two;
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile;	and if you think that his stomach is cooled down, and the meat does not cook, and one sees swell the skin, then on the skin I grant cautery over the stomach, as it is said before, and another over the liver, and another over the mouse to all the cauterized clavicles;
et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After care, let the wound heal until it is well.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the flesh that is called “thel”
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit;	When you cut the hellebore, if you heat up the cautery that seems like a razor, and then put it all on fire on the chopped hellebore;
et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort;	and I leave so much your hand that the cauterization comes to the birth of the vein, from which it is not cut short;
fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit;	do this once or twice, and if there is much hellebore, then cauterize each one as we have said;
aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez;	after the treatments with beneficial herbs until they are healed;
et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	and if you cauterize with a large cauldron over fire, it will be more helpful.
de plaie mal curee	of a badly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot bear cutting or opening, which we will tell you in your place, so comes a disease that cannot be cured except by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	If there is no outlet for the wind, and it is agitated and vomits pus and moisture, then it must be given an extremely subtle treatment, and you must know exactly how much of the treatment is perfect.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing;	After heat the cauldron that looks like a razor, and pour it into the fistula according to the quantity that it has entered, and restart the cauldron as long as that heart is infected and rotten, once or II or III, according to the quantity of the remedy required;
et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	and protect yourself from the nerves that are inside, and great veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans;	If the fistula goes to the core of the bladder and intestine, protect yourself from these nerves, and do not make fire except in the flesh, and think that it is not useless;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement;	After you have healed the nerve as long as it is healthy, and if the nerves are scarred, and the matter is ossified for a long time, then know that the nerve is completely healed;
et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font;	and if the materials are not osteous, know that the bones are three, and the bone is corrupted at its root.
et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	and so with one of these that we will say in his place.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit;	When the pain of frost comes with rain and a heavy wind, and does not take the shape of a woman, then you must make a fire on either side at the clove-joint that we have mentioned above;
et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	and if we cauterize it in the middle, then there will be three cauterizations in a line, and greater help will be done.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce;	When the bladder is soft and weak from frost and moisture, so that the patient retenes urine, then you make a fire in the part opposite the bladder, where the hair of the penis begins, and one on each side, and let each cauterization be as long as a finger.
et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing;	and let me cut the back, where you have been pricked.
et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	and let the cauterization be made according to the shape described above.
de la marris	of the mare
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde;	When the marrow is cold and moist, and will not allow conception, and the flowers are decaying and late in maturing;
et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor:	and when they come, such great pain is felt:
adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos;	then you must make three cauterizations around the loins, as we said above in the cautery of the bladder, and a cauterization on the back;
et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	and let the cauterization be made by claving, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hindquarter
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble;	When the viscous moisture descends into the hip joint box, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and the sign is that the leg is longer than the other when measured together;
et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle;	and find the line of the hip joint department, so that you can cauterize the patient on the hip joint box at the circle-like cautery, and sign in front of the line around the box as it comes back, so that the box is within the circle;
et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	And if there is such fire cautery as that which we use to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs;	If this fire cautery is not present, then make three cauterizations with the olive oil, and also make it completely as all the keys;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healthy.
de la dolor de la hainche	for the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene:	When the pain comes in the hip joint, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we have said in the dislocation, and the cure does not work, and the illness is old:
adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	then you must purge the patient of great humors with foul pills, or other bad-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere;	After that, make a fire cautery;
et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres:	and the method of the cautery should be according to two methods:
c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	it is as follows together hot medicines and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz:	Fire cautery if it is according to the manners of which one is such:
que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire;	To cauterize the hip of the horse III triangular cauterizes according to this form, and you make it deep and wide, and have between each cauterize a space whose size is that of two fingers, and let the cauterizes be olive-colored;
aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	No one does fire cautery in the middle on the head of the hip, for there are three according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche;	And if you see, if the cauterization is with a circle of fire that we have said before in the dislocation of the hip;
mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	But do it in this way that the circle contains all the hip, and all the thickness of the leg is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way it is done in sciatica, when the pain remains in the hip and does not reach the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc;	And if it comes only to the thigh and leg, you do two cauterizes here where the patient says that the pain holds him back, and one cauterize above the ankle three fingers, on the left side a little bit;
et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur;	and let the cauterization of the knife, and let burn the thickness of the skin.
et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two or three fingers or four or five away from the wound, cauterize it at one of those points with the fire cautery called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus;	And if they are qualified, let them do it more often.
et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	and if he says that the pain is in his knee and goes towards his thigh, then you make a cauterization with the knife or circular cautery, and be careful in all your cauterizations so that you do not leave them for too long; neither do you burn the nerves nor the large arteries, and do not cause the patient too much damage and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I have seen many who have made a cauterization on the heel of the foot and left it so long that the leg was completely swollen, and the bones as well, and it became pierced and rotten throughout the bones.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a solution for the stomach which has brought death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two places together, make a fire cauterization in one and in the other, according to this way.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce;	And the wise men say in the cauterization of the hip, as for this manner, you should do it and make it at the top just as thick as a fingernail or a little less, and between the cheeks and also from one cheek to another with a space the size of a fingernail;
et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait;	and let there be between them two bars, and also as knots, and I have one of iron well made;
et c’est li forme:	this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit;	And let it be heated until it is quite red and cool it down, and then put it on the hip bone of the sick person, and turn it around the small of the back;
et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors;	and the fire cautery once more and let him rest for three days;
et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens;	then do an ointment of butter, and leave the open wound long;
aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the course of ointment until it is well.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent;	Albucasis says that we use little of this cautery because of its danger, and those who use it little;
et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	and all the same this is a good cautery which can bear it, and where it afflicts him.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi;	The medicine-burning cauterizes if you make an instrument from which the end of the margin of the door extends, and it is of brass or iron to a long wall, and there are two of us, and each has the quantity of the thickness of a finger.
et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	and be placed above and below, and join together according to this shape:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche;	After you have put the box on the patient's back and made sure that it is steady, and you hold your hand very close to the patient's back.
aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After you have placed the two circles of hot metal, which are heated in a firepot, and leave them for an hour, and allow the patient to feel the heat and the burning:
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu;	For it will produce the same effect as fire.
