puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	Then he removes the suction cups and lets the oil strain day and night, and the ligament becomes looser, so that you must remove it slowly.
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	Then he removes the ligature after day and night, and if you see the oil recover, it is good;
se ce non;	if not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	then start again with plaster and bandages and the ligature and suction cups as long as it is healthy.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The tearing of woven cloth.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When disruptions come in the woven cloth, then open, and comes paper-like grains as if a resin seed, and is predictable to see;
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	then if you see it covered, the overlay is such that you push a needle into the root of the part almost up to the top, and then push another needle where the thread is doubled in the part of the rope;
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and pierce her, and leave the first needle according to arrangement;
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then cut the thread in two places and tie one end of the loop, then tighten it well, then remove the needle and put another moistened thread in abundance of wax;
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and leave it until the thread sounds with the loop, then treat the oil with comforting things until the wound is healed;
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and no time the wound is restricted by a circular bandage of cloth each part of a circle, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the hair is very fine, if you pierce it with a very fine spittle that comes from oil in perfection, and draw away the moistened albuginous and cut the hair, and insert it soon;
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then remove it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	with oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease which is called "alkunah" is only water that is gathered in oil, resembling water descending, and it is not water.
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the way of the appearance of this chapter is that you make sit the patient on one side bare and straight, then take the head between your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the bow come to your fingers;
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then let him sit down, and do not kneel or bend your back, and look at the patient's things as if he were alone;
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not sit down, know that it is acute, and the sitting of the bow should not be bare as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	if you sit the patient between your hands, then take the thin spatchula and put it on the horny membrane I hole by the continuation of the conjunctive with the horny membrane and the crown, until the bow comes out;
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it is out, let it be distilled in hot acrid honey, or acrid water or fenugreek boiled and honey, then let other cures be used until it is cured;
des aigues de l’oil	with the water of the oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have the appearance of needles in the incision, and what is necessary to pierce.
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	for in the work according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is necessary that you sit the patient between your hands crossed, away from the light by the sun, and press the healthy oil very strongly;
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	then put the paper of oil in your left hand if the hairs are left-handed, or in your right hand if the hairs are right-handed;
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	then take in your right hand, if the hairs are left-handed, the instrument which is called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the hairs are right-handed;
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	then put the tip of the instrument at the base of the hair by its thick end in the blubber of oil in the part of the lesser larmier, then bottle the instrument which is called "almagda" firmly, and turn your hand around until it pierces into the blubber of oil, and feel that almagda comes to the hollow thing;
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and the measure of the vein of mercury should be at the perfect measure of the space that is from the prunella to the end of blackness;
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and this is the crown of oil;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the corned skin, and then put the instrument up to the water where it is, and then express one vein after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he faints now, then see the patient in front of him and the instrument on his oil.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	Then rest for a little, and the water rises again the second vein, put the force with the instrument, and when it is well stuck and does not rise anymore, then draw out mercury lightly by turning your hand back and forth;
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then put a little of the green thread into the water, and leave it from that oil inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put on one side the oily oil where or another moist thing in oil and a lot of water, and bind with healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now then, and those who are of our sect, let us put on common broied with a lot of water.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the alum cannot enter the oil because of its hardness, for there are some men who have too hard hairs, then you must squeeze the instrument which is called "alberit", from which this form comes:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And then pierce the conjunctive only, and do not go too deep with the needle, but make it fine, then draw out mercury, as we have said;
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a dark place to sleep, so that he sleeps on his back.
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and be free of all movement, and eat light food, and do not move his head to the right or left, and bind him according to his condition for about three days.
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	then release him in that same dark house and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then he remakes the bandage until the seventh day.
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	and it is not necessary that you do this in the hour of the cure or afterwards, but it is necessary that you prepare it beforehand, so that water does not mount up inside him.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	if the abscesses are fresh, you should remove the poultice before the seventh day and apply the poultice from someone who soothes an abscess.
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	and when it is calm, if he does not lie down the face up, so that he may not see any more, and be in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	And then out of the house little by little, and turn back to his case;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and know that no one should meddle in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us who was from Jericho, who told us that in his country there is such a thing as an earthquake, which sucks up water, but nevertheless I have never seen it in our land, nor have I ever heard of it in the books of the ancients;
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the signs of the shapes of almagda, for he who does not know them may see them;
et soient d’arain proprement:	and let them be of pure bronze;
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And may the head of the two of this very subtleness be, and behind three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the neck from the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	And no one is born or dies of various kinds of horses, from which there are none who seem to be scorpions at the mouth of stones;
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if there is any of this or that it has green wax of fox, and if there is any good-colored wax.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In this case of the wax that is good, and not green, it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands towards the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and open his nostrils, and pour the ointment into these waxes, and massage them;
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	and then you may take this that you have prepared with a thin spatula from one side, as long as you know that this wax is all bone;
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if there remains nothing of it that you cannot cover, then open it with a very light and thin instrument, so that nothing stays behind;
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and let him stretch out, or absess, as it is necessary;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if they are malicious abscesses, then hurry and cauterize as soon as the skin is stained and all the waxes are boneless, then pour or do not pour easily and quickly and run water.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If there is no pain, and moisture comes up to the throat, know that he is well.
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if there is no perforation like it should, know that he has a bone split above, so that the tool does not cut properly:
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	then you must put a piece of linen thread, about an inch thick, between each tooth, and bind it tightly with the hands, and leave some space or less between each knot;
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and put the patient's teeth in linen thread at his finger ends, and draw it through his nose while smelling until it comes out of the nose into the mouth;
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many times do this to the child while he is in school, and it is an easy thing for him who does it;
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold the head that comes out of the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and take one after another while we are threading the linen thread;
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Make it as long as you know that the new one has corrupted this thread, then treat the child, wash the blood, and soak the hair in Egyptian ointment, and put it back on the neck immediately as before;
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Fai ceu three or more days, as long as the ointments corrupt all that is delayed from the hair;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then put on the neck a twine of thread some days as long as it is healthy, and if it needs dry medicine, then use it;
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	And this is the form of the instrument to purify the head, so that one distills the oils and the medicines on the neck:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And be of silver or gold, resembling a lamp opened, like a twine, and lead it also;
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you see, then make a closed twine, and be the instrument plain to purify the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and always hold the head so it doesn't move when they heat oil or any other liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the neck from the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times a disease that is called "telul" appears at the head and grows and becomes very large, so much so that it can be seen with the eye.
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	And for this reason you must hold the head still at the beginning and put the fire or burning medicine on it;
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if you delay covering it until it is very large, take care if it is hard, of its color, of its poor sense:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	don't ever touch it with iron because it is an infected abscess, for when you cover it up there comes great evil to the patient;
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of poor color, and you see that it can be completely covered, so cover the patient well with drying and restraining things;
quant li neis est copez et cosus	what the eyes are cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	It is known that when a solution of continuance comes to one of these cartilage ovulations, it does so little, otherwise in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is therefore necessary that someone come who, if the wound is fresh throughout his body,
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then he fixes the two lips to a stitch, and then he cares for it until he is well;
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are torn from one side to the other, it is necessary that you peel all their parts until they heal, then join the two lips to a stitch, and tighten them, and powder them with dragon's blood and burned incense;
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put on the powders a piece of resin of some sort or other resin that sticks together, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then care for it with ointment until it is well.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The way to stitch so is that you join the wound:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we have said in stitching the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	ou par fil, if as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	With hands at home, inside the lips there are hard, resembling seeds of times, and small and large;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	Then it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut each in two, and take them with pincers and chop them into parts;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then apply the fire after the incision of vitriol, until the blood is stopped;
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let it rest, and treat the wound with dry things until it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	of the teeth
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Often a tooth comes out on the gums, which the old people call "albulus";
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	if it is necessary that you hold it with pliers and cut off the tooth at the root, and let the blood run out;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then apply the fire of vitriol, or other powdered substances that bind and dry up;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if it returns after the incision, and many times happens, if the cope the second time, and cauterize.
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not return after the cauterization;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the forms of the instruments to cope.
des sordens	of the orders
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	No joints are assembled to the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and rough;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and no tooth is black and yellow and rotten, as long as the decay comes to the gum, and the teeth are stinking;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	if you make the patient sit between your hands, and his joints are in your holy place, and expose the teeth or scars as much as possible, so that nothing is delayed;
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and then make it black and green, and yellow and other colors, until they are clean;
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if one bone is in the first ratio, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if not, then begin again on the second day and third part, until you have all of them;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that the teeth have different shapes of instruments to cut, according to what the operation shows, because the scissor which one uses to cut hair has other shapes than those which one uses to cut flesh;
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these forms and others are with you equipped.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when you heal the tooth's pain that you wait to draw it out as long as you can, because one should not do this at all;
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	because it is a substance of high moisture so that one does not have an excuse to draw it out.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	And now when the patient is forced to extract it, you must be certain about the tooth that hurts.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the pain leaves the patient, and he thinks that the tooth is healthy, and he makes the good tooth drawn out;
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and wherever it does not go away with medicine, as long as the evil is removed, because we have already tried to do this for these elderly people;
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are certain of the tooth that hurts, so it is necessary that you scorch the gum in all directions with strong spittle;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then dip it in your two hands or small nails at the first hole and hole, until it is well loosened, then firmly secure the nails;
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and place the head of the sick person between your knees, and hold him securely so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After removing the tooth correctly without breaking it, if it does not come out, take one of these tools and push it into each side lightly, and move it around as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if it is pierced and blood comes out, fill it with cloth where the hole is;
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if you hold it tightly with small nails so that it does not break while you are holding it;
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and it is necessary to cover the wound above the gums so as not to disrupt the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And you should be careful not to break it and leave a part of it, and let the patient feel more pain from the root than from the first one.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And you must not do so in the same way as the ignorant surgeon does, who, through his haste and recklessness, often breaks the chariot, and cannot administer what we have described;
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but bring about by the fire of that great disease through the roots which it holds back, or through the chariot which it breaks, as we have often seen;
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is drawn, wash the place with wine or water and string;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and let it dry of blood which comes out, for that often happens, if one employs the place of vitriol;
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if that does not work, then use fire;
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shape of the instrument which first prepares the tooth is such that it has long points and thick handles so that it does not double up as you draw out the tooth;
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be strong limbs so that they do not bend when pulled, and well-made iron, and let them have teeth to hold fast.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root is still at the trellis, you should put cotton wet with oil on the joint or two, as long as the leg is soft, because the nails that are called "algefri" seem like a 병;
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and inside they make like a file and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, then you must take off the whole tooth, and put the instrument that is called 'althali', that is a chisel; this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And be far away from sharp things so that it does not break, and the root jumps because of that, it is good.
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	If not, if you help yourself with all the tools, by which the forms come here after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps himself with this instrument that has two heads, from which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front in the rasion of teeth, and this instrument which seems a big pliers, whose is this form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And be sure that no tool can break it, and know that most of the tools that are inside are;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other tools, which are not counted;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the master sages subtlety tries on their own instrument according to what their art and the disease of the patient show them, for there are many diseases or the old man does not teach an instrument for the diversity of them; and if it does not break the chariot or other bones, or he falls, if he seeks the instruments that suit him, I have told you, and helps with gestures, by which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be big and firmly holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but can hold and remove it.
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then return the head to the place of medicine that is suitable for this, and if there is a pus in the bone, and it is small, then the cure with all this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the teeth appear not in accordance with the natural form of the jaw, and the shape is ugly, especially in young women, it is necessary that you know whether the root is attached to the tooth or not; it does not fit into its place, and one cannot nail or file it:
adonques lou raie;	then the extraction:
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is attached to the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is similar to a small pick, and which is made of iron;
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cap fits tight and tight by the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it seems that it can be filed, then take a file with this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is also like the file from which one makes needles;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and at intervals rub the tooth with a little water so that it does not move until it comes out.
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	Then the plane at the end to any razor, and its density is too hard and it bleeds the tongue, then you should rub the sharp edge until it is even, so that it does not bleed the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth loosens...
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the tooth is loose, either by pounding or by pulling, and the patient cannot bear pressure on it without hurting, and you have treated them with restrictives, and that does not help;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	if you can restrain it with a gold wire, for the silver wire turns green and puces, but the gold never moves;
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the wire be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the quantity of space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you see how to smooth the dense bones, then take the string and double-knot it between the two dense bones, then put the heads between the dense bones, if there are one or more, until you get them smoothly up to the healthy tooth on the other side;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then start wrapping again until you get to the part where you started, and slowly and carefully remove your hand, so that it does not move.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and make sure that your grip is on the root of the tooth so that he cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then take the heads with pliers, and join them together, and put them between the healthy tooth, and so that he does not hurt his tongue;
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then leave it tight as long as it can stay in place, and if it slips or the thread breaks, hold it with another thread;
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	if it stays and serves for all its time, and this is the form of the upper and lower sides, and the appearance of the two upper ribs and the two lower ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when a tooth falls out, if it is put back in its place again and again, as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and do not meddle with those who are not wise and patient, and never make the shape of a tooth out of a piece of hay; and put it back in its place where it failed, and hold it fast as we have said, and stay and serve for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of copper the tongue of the language
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Never is there a tongue that comes out of the mouth or nature, which one bears in one's body;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by accident of a sore burn;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the work is such that you open the mouth of the sick person and put your hand on his chin, and hold his tongue down;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	and then cut the nerves long, as long as the tongue is dislocated from its socket, and if there is any hardness or numbness, and this is sudden pain from a wound, so he pulls out the nerve and cuts the ligaments.
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and be careful that the incision is not too deep, lest the artery be cut.
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done so, raise the level of salt water and cool it, then put a patch of linen on the tongue.
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and rub the disease on each night so that the hole does not close.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if fever comes, then put vinegar on the spot.
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if it does not go away, then apply fire to the skin with a white hot spark, which is good for this.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then treat with other treatments until it heals,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see a red or black or hard color so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it because it is leprosy;
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is slanting to the left, and there is moisture, then pour the ointment, and wash with a thin sponge, and deliver from one side to the other;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if it does not go to your ointment, put it on vitriol until it is stained, and then return to your ointment while you take all of it;
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then lift up the head from there and from rope, and heal him with other treatments until he is well.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	No one should put his finger or hand into his mouth, which are called "godaths", and they are properly called "amandres"; and when you heal them, as we have said in the division of them, and they are not healed, take care:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If the abscess is small and has a pale color, then do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and its root is large, then do not touch it with iron, also for the removal of blood from the wound;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but let it alone until it dies, and then you will remove it, or it would break by itself;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is of a pale color and its root is thin, then prepare the instrument to cover it, but first see that the abscess is warm and calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then make the patient sit in the sun, and his shoulders are parallel to the ground, and he opens his mouth and places his thumb between his hands, and presses his tongue against all the instrument, so it is shaped like this:
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and be of silver or thin gold as well as our knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	And then press the tongue to all this instrument, and you see the abscess, take the scalpel and put it in amber, and drive it up above what you can.
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and then remove any threads with it, then the cover to the instrument, so that this is the form, that seems one's force;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and allways the head are corbed, and one place another, and they are very good, and is made of iron ind or forge:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	If you do not have this instrument present, if you take the handle with pliers, so that there is a form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And let be trenchant on one side, and on other side no;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and when you have covered one of the amber, so cover the other according this same manner, and after the incision gargarize the patient with hot water, and cold and easily, and let them rest until they stop bleeding, if gargarize the patient with cooked pomegranate juice, or cooked apple leaves, or similar things, as long as the wound is cleaned;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then treat until he is well.
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	and never do any other abscesses in the throat than the two mandibles, unless they are very much like the two mandibles.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman of an abscess that was lying within her throat, that is to say, one small abscess.
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and I had well closed all the throat, so that the woman could not breathe by the conduit which was stopped up, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had stayed thus for one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had risen two rain-cycles through the two apertures where the drainage was coming from.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I hastened then a little, and put in one of the incisions, then I tore it open again, and put in a large portion of bowstring.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then I refitted another part on the other hole where the abscess was, and closed his mouth and pressed his tongue.
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	after I put the ointment on these abscesses, I poured some of it out, and only a little blood came out.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and then I removed the tube from her throat, and now she began to drink water and wine, and I kept cutting this abscess for a long time;
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscess reopened, filling up the space that I had emptied, until it was very large;
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	then I put a stop to it and cauterized it in her throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	after that it stopped hurting.
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and then I left these parts, and only God knows what will happen to them after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the wound heals up, and she is gone and far away, then it is called "perpendicular.
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if she has had a large and round belly, then it is called "ve.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When she is healed as we said in the division, and the healing does not benefit her, and you see that the abscesses are calm, and they are subtle, so it is necessary that you cut them.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and this one who is round and assembled and is not far away;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is bloody or a purple color or black, so you avoid the incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger with the eye disease.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is necessary therefore, when you see it, according to the way that I have said, of its blenching and its length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue to the instrument of which we have spoken above;
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Then place the ring in its hole, and split it open, and cut it with two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two mandibles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And you must not cover more than the excess that is beyond the natural term.
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you cover more, it hurts the throat and speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use what we said in the incision of the two testicles, and heal it until it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has doubt about covering; then you must use fire cautery on the painful part.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the way of fire cautery is sharp water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is that the patient puts his head in your place, and then he presses the tongue to the instrument that we said or fire cautery, and mixes with sharp vinegar so that it is not too thick or too clear;
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and use this tool's maneuver, from which comes this form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	and put the head in a bunch or hair where one puts the medicine, like the bunches of a spoon, and place the instrument on all the medicine on the wound;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient be lying on his side, so that his saliva and mucus run from his mouth into the medicine, so that he does not choke in the throat, and burn it;
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then keep your hand over all the medicine and press it against the eye, the quantity of half an hour, until you see it become calm and the medicine's stinging is relieved;
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see it, take cotton and wrap it over any instrument, and moisten the cotton with the medicine, and dip the instrument into all the cotton in the chain above, until the cotton dries on the eye;
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, until the fire-cautery is perfect, then leave it to dry, and see after III or IV days or V;
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to prepare the medicine fire-cautery, if it is prepared, and after the fire-cautery rinse it with cotton soaked in medicine, and clean what is inside of the medicine;
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be dipped in cold water, and be cured by gargling until it is well;
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This cure is safer than incision, except for cautery.
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	if she is cured by fumigation in this way, take calamus and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and yarrow and similar herbs, and put them all together or any of them in a pot, and put it there like this, and make it boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot is well glued with strong earth, and dip the tool in this way:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	and be of silver or gold, and be one of the shoulders squeezed in the mouth of the patient as long as the vapor rises to the vein through the tube, until the vein is numb;
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	after it has started again, often, until the vein is dried up, and you keep it from happening at the beginning of the entrance of the abscess, for many things have happened;
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not make such a fire that it burns at the base of the apophelis.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, then take a knife and put it in the patient's mouth at the base of the apophelis so that the mouth does not get too hot.
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	For the knife of the ape does not make the steam very hot in the mouth, and this is a good treatment that saves both together.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Often there is an object stuck in the throat, or a bone, or nothing.
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	so that you can take what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the object;
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and if what is not open for you and has been pushed back into the throat, then you must make the patient vomit so that the meat is cooked in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	By chance if the thing disturbs by vomiting.
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	Or if the patient swallows a sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a piece of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and he puts it in his throat and then swallows it;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes to the place, if it disturbe, and then pull hard;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come out well from what we have said, then take an instrument to hit according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instrument be bent at the end so that it can enter more easily into the throat, and lift up the head;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, that it does not come to him, and do not push the bone inside;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and move the patient so that he can breathe, so that the thing does not disturb him;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	if the bottle is swallowed, or he draws it out with all the instrument evenly, as long as it is strong.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the fluid from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	No medicine is more important than the one I have mentioned in the division, by the cure of medicines;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	And when that does not benefit, then look at the patient's throat in the sunlight, so you can press the tongue to the instrument I have told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the fluid, if you draw it out with a small hook or tiny claws that are worth nothing.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, then take a knife, and put it in the throat of the patient, then blow on or cut with the blade, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is coughing up water every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and let it fall into the throat, and move it from side to side often with his hand;
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	And if soon after swallowing the water feels cold, then turn around quickly.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if she does not sneeze as we have said, then make the patient sniff smoke with the instrument I mentioned in the fumes of the wine;
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	do this many times, for it will make her sneeze without a runny nose.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the way of smoking if you squeeze a pot where it has charcoal visible, and let the pot be covered with a coverlet pierced in the middle, and in that perforation is the head of the instrument.
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then pour in your smoking, and let the patient put the head of the cane in his mouth, and close his mouth so that the smoke does not go out, but comes to the blood;
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the blood will come now, and if it does not come, then recommence the smoking with many times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and suffer the patient to have thirst, and drink salt things and bitter, and do not drink water;
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then it is the duty of healing that he is done by this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the form of the instrument to see how it treats the blood, yes, when you can see it, similar to twisted hooks so that they can enter the throat;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and give a look to the beak of care, and I had harshness of lime, so that whoever takes it, she cannot let go;
et vez ci la forme:	and see this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the scalpels for the abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	The shape of the mouth of an abscess is, according to what the memory comes after one and another in this book, and are diverse in piercing and cutting;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and this is in two ways, that one is in its own shape, and of what he holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the joints where they are twisted.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess at the top is different from that at the base, and the abscess at the twisted part is different from that which comes in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if to abscesses it does not have to pierce, as long as the bow is dead according to its achievement;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if of such that it comes to pierce when it is cut, and do not die according to its achievement, as an abscess which are delicate joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come in delicate joints, and one lets them remain pus-filled inside, by chance if the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, this is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Or the abscess is a delicate limb, and if you delay the piercing as long as it is dead, it will harm the principal limb;
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	If he is delved down to the foundation, if it is perceived that it is dead;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is not necessary that you pierce the abscess cruelly after having accomplished the digestion, so that the one who is delved down to the foundation does not putrefy completely and remains within, and comes out with a fistula;
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot heal in great terms.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is necessary that you know the hour of piercing the abscess which is dead according to the accomplishment, and it is when the pain is calm, and the departure of the fever, and the decrease of the pain and rubor, and the tension and the keenness of the head of the abscess, and the other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and it is necessary that you make sit the piercing or more dependent place of the abscess, and where it opens much;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and the piercing of the long pipe of the heart, and the abscesses are in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and in all even where there is no pleurisy.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who bleed, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when the abscess is in the flesh, if it pricks let the piercing be until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce ahead of this, if you stretch the pipe of its blood, and it is plain of mud of waste;
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and perhaps the lips become hardened and the depth of it becomes deep.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to any abscess that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to which the members have need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is necessary that you bring small abscesses, small holes;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in great abscesses, great holes, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if at such abscesses it is necessary to cut the kur and cover;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it has become soft as cloth, and is worn out, if you make it like you make boils:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if they are of those that are split into three angles, and if they are of those that one also copes with as the skin of the myrtle, like abscesses of arms.
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if they are of those for which one makes a ring size, and other sizes and similar copes.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who do not have a head, like a superficial abscess, you must pierce it clearly;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has a large boil, and you pierce it, if you do not extract all of the boil at once, but extract a part of it;
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then stop the abscess just until the next day, then extract nothing else primarily;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	do this again and again with great effort, until all the boil has come out;
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	usually the disease is of little virtue, or a woman bearing, or small children, or old honourable people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	Those who do not have a head, like an abscess on the skin, it is necessary that you pierce it clearly; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and has a great boil, and you pierce it, if you do not draw all the boil at once, but draw some part of it; then stop the abscess until the next day, then draw no more; do this many times in succession, as the boil comes out completely; but if the patient is of feeble virtue, or a woman bearing, or small children, or old men decayed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Begin therefore this treatment with great caution, and when you have pricked your abscess, if the wound is small, wash it.
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a long, straight scar, if you apply linen or old cotton.
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess and there are many ruptures, you must pierce each one with a tent so that they touch each other.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have torn a part of the skin with the abscess, and you have wrapped it with a cloth, you must fill it with dry cotton or straw of linen without moisture, and bind it firmly for three days.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply the ointment, and treat with medicine until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is a strong fever that arises from the opening, then administer cold water and do it quickly, and wet the cloth, and place it on the opening many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the blood loss persists, apply treatment and the powders I have mentioned in this book, and if it is a long scar or an abscess that is very painful, you must put linen and towels soaked in wine and oil on them.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in this state, and his legs are fleshy, it is necessary that you dip the blankets in water and oil, or in wine and oil until the third day, as we have said;
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then wash the abscess and dry it and heal it, as it should be, until it is healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this it is necessary that he recognizes completely in the treatment of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	Or you have said to me how one must go before in the treatment of abscesses, and see the paste.
des soros	sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or treat small sores, and they are handled by us so that they are in webs, also as the neck of a goose, and there are many resemblances.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There is some that is fat and such where there is also moisture as feathers;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and if it is this kind which is hard and bony at the cutting, and there is no doubt that his artery does not make opposition.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the waist so that you test all the instrument called "intramuscular", from which the form comes after, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, and it goes up into the long leg.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when moisture is empty, if it scalds nothing the hair which contains that moisture, for it returns immediately as one leaves nothing;
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	If not, use water and salve, and apply to the wound, and leave it until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and those who have been pricked apply ointment to them, as they are delayed due to nit;
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then dip the cotton again on the second day, and the salve, as long as you know that the nit does not remain;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply ointment to the wound with what is suitable, until it is healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess does not go down quickly according to this form, then cut it;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and throw your scabs, and scorch all parts of it, and put all your treatment outside the coat or where it is;
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the artery is against you, do what I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also make an incision on the abscess if it is painful, and with a scalpel and a curette as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut on the abscess that is painful and moist, for it is lighter because there is little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if some of these abscesses or head or there is no moisture, and those are the only ones that I saw or head of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and I found the abscess as a large, sharp, and white stone, and could not break it;
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if any of them had been cut, one would have done the same wound as a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses that come out of the head, they are those that come from the ears and roots of the hair, the opening should be completely closed so that the bow does not get stuck;
et les cure si com il covient.	And treat them as it should be done.
des scrophules	of the scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times have they come with abscesses to the throat, and have removed the lumps, and have had boils, and never come to another place or sore, and are rotten, and infected one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scab is properly inside its shell, like the nose and abscess on the head, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And the appearance of these scabs is varied.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that are malign and do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in that which you see of good disposition in the chest, and appears similar to the color of the flesh, and is mute from each part and is not attached to the neck neither to the artery nor to the duct, and is not deeply rooted.
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	if it is necessary that you chop it from above, and peel each part, and the two lips of the mouth are turned up to one side, if you need it, as we have said in the treatment of the chest with scars.
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and cut it little by little, and be sure that you do not cover the nerve or the vein, nor is there any risk of cutting the tongue or causing a wound that the hands do not escape, and do not look too far ahead, so that you do not cover anything you are not supposed to.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or the artery, and it does not allow you to sew it, then put vinegar in the wound, or some powders that stop the blood, and draw the wound out.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and leave it until the abscesses are calm, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood has stopped flowing, if you return to your work, as long as you finish it off;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then inspect your little finger for any small bumps, if there are none, scrape and wash them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is great root of the scar, then it only comes to scrape that scar in its root, but let it hang by a strong thread, and let it fall without any harm;
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	then employ cotton wool dipped in olive oil, then clean it up.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you catch the whole scrofula, it is necessary that you join together the two lips of the wound and sew them up, so that there is no delay because of its great size.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you listen to cover the root of it, and draw it out firmly, and sew it up as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	These scars that have excess fluid, pierce where it is opening and dying;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and pierce in the same way as that which is said before, depending on, then I spread tendres with olive oil and similar things, so that it corrupts those who are delayed from corruption;
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well dressed, if the healing ointment comes into contact with it, as long as it is healthy.
de squinance	squinance
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients spoke of the treatment of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I have never seen it done in our land, and it is written in their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those who have laryngitis, it is necessary that the opening of the throat called "epiglotte" be removed;
