et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and do not use this, for all the veins and the blood of the patient are hot in his mouth or throat or in two mandibles.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the patient is in the vein of the neck, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis so that the strangulation which comes from the obstruction does not occur.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to remove the epiglotte, we should make a cut of three circles or four small cuts from the edge, between the two circles or by the quantity of the cut in the cartilage; do not cut it in the cartilages.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and if their lips are not suitable for cutting the epiglottis, there is no char, and the vessels are long from it.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is afraid, then it is necessary that he extends the skin of the throat to the very end, and then cuts the meat as far as it comes to the cheekbone.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid the blood vessels, if you see nothing, and then apply the salve, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and is proven by the cutting of the vein of the cheek which sprouted from the place that was broken, and by the loss of speech.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the open wound as a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed by which one doubts about strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the meat, and the whole shoulder under the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and administer medicines which cause a growth of hair, as long as he is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says: 'Do not make this cut until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be dying, and the failure causes him to lose his voice.'
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then wrap the epiglottis around it so that the patient cannot move it, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and to command the elder to leave the wound open as long as the disease is gone, and it has passed in three days or four. And then he commanded to stitch up the wound and heal, until it was healed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a damsel take a knife and put it in her throat, and she cut through the chisel of the pommel;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to heal her, and I found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had issued from it, and I knew well that she had not cut a vein or an artery; the blood came forth from the mouth because of the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, sewed the wound, and healed it until it was well;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and didn't come to the damsel except she was red in color, and returned after her condition;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	for I fear that in cutting off the epiglottis there will be no pain.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	the abscesses are called "gastric hernias", and there is a large abscess in the color of a mustard seed, and it is very common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	and is according to two ways:
naturez, et accidens;	natural, and accidental;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	where nature has no fault.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental one is according to two ways, of which one seems like fat to us, and the other way seems like an abscess that comes from our arteries;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and he has fear, and it is not good to operate on fire without first making sure of the small one, and testing and searching all the instruments;
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you know how to fix it like I don't know how, and can't do anything at all, if the cup, as we use cups, and treat him with everything he needs, if there is any left.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And look well after it, and treat it properly, so that it is completely cured.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways of doing this, all of which I will describe.
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And it is necessary that I say all the differences there are between us and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that dislocation is hot and fiery, as long as the fever has passed and the blistering is done;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Then the fever and the heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the cup there is no heat or fever or pain, and it heals itself, which is its own sac, and it begins as a scar, and becomes bigger;
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and according to two appearances, either grass, or moist, and much of a color are so as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to treat our condition, you must first test and inquire about all the instruments that are called "entromissoire", according to their form or the paste that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the way of testing the abscesses is that you press out or more moist liquid than you find in the abscess, and twist your thumbs little by little until you feel that the instrument has penetrated, then stop according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then remove the instrument, and take care not to hurt yourself.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	if it runs quickly with moisture, which color it has, then do the same as I said for the other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the instrument no moisture comes out, know that it is fat, so do it in a cross shape and take it with tweezers, and scrape it slightly from each side and save the cot or where it lies;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot draw it out whole, then draw it out piece by piece so that nothing stays behind.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it will return to us many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if there is a little bit of it, and it does not cause you pain, then employ some corrosive water to extract the wound, and put something soothing on it, and give it other treatments until it heals;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if it is large, cut off the two corners of the wound, and treat what causes it to hurt;
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the vein is opposite or another way, then hurry and employ the place of vitriolic broich, and let it stand for two or three days until the wound festers, and rest the blister in the blood;
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to copper what has been left behind by the blood.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See here the forms of the intruding instruments, and they are of three manners:
grans et moien et petit;	large and mean and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three quarters that are called 'albaret', and one that is called 'breb', and they are of three manners:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, mean, and small, so as to encircle the abscesses of fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles used to count sorceles, and they are of yellow brass, or iron, or silver, and those that are made of yellow brass are more proven to sound black, so as to encircle the corbiculae of fistula;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three manners:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	large, mean, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the apertures.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The forms of the hooks are of many appearances, as you will see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	large, small, and tiny
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if one has three corbecs of three ways;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if one has three corbecs, and are also of three ways;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if one has two corbecs, and once of a corbec, and are of three ways;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all of these are necessary in their places.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these should be sharp, and of some I have who only cut from one side, so that when you skin them, you can cut the vein or the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and of these introducers are the alems replied in many, so that the patient does not lose them at the opening of the abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	and there are three ways:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	large, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and don't use any but if in its place like legs, arms, mammary glands, and shoulders, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and never make any other instrument small, resembling scurf of blisters, according to this form, so that one does not burn with fire:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	The chief of these cuts are sharp, and some do not cut more than one side, from which we peel the skin so that we do not touch the vein or nerve; and these intrusions are placed in many ways, so that the patient does not lose them when opening the abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and middle, as you see; and we use them only in the leathery part, as legs, arms, mammary glands, and arms, and similar things; and never do we make another instrument small, resembling blades, according to this form, so that we stop the blood:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	The breasts of some men become inflamed when they are infected and appear like the breasts of women.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and those who must treat them, if it is appropriate according to this form of that line: b. g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scratch the fat, and apply medicine to the wound by wrapping it, then join the two lips of the wound with sutures, and treat it until it is healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if his breast falls down, and becomes soft because of its size like a woman's, if it is made into two ridges on top, by two resembling clefts:
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	from which one is held by the other at the end of one and the other, so that the greater line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line. b . g .;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then peel off the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about suturing and powders, and whatever is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made, so that the patient does not rest, or because of the evacuation of blood, then you must fill the wound with wet cotton impregnated with an astringent;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until the remaining skin and fat has dried up, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of the hips of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	The pustules that come from the glutes are handled with care or they have ribs, and if there is only one that contains moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this shape, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all of the bow that is in the pustule is empty, then employ cotton wool, and leave it there for another day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment as soon as it is healthy:
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the pustule is like a wart, then cut it as we have said in cutting warts, and if there is bow in the wound, then apply fire cautery as we have described before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is torn and the skin that is above it is tightened, then many abscesses come, and also they go to the escaped vein and abscess;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if the incision is deep as much as for the artery, if it is long the abscess completely.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel it on both sides, if you feel extraction.
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is for the vein, if it is to be cut apart.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolishness to cover this abscess, and most of all when it is dislocated in the armpit and in the throat and in other places, and there are many.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore it is convenient to remove the cure of iron, and that which is at the top also has to be removed, and in that which is swollen with an artery, do so from above the skin.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then operate the waist like one person, and separate the artery from the threads well, until it is uncovered;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	then stick in one needle, and make it pierce up to the other side, and extract the artery with a double thread according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries which are in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	and then point to the place that is between the two ties of an intromitter as long as there is no tie there, and loosen the aphistma.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then administer the cure for a bowel rupture as long as the link remains intact;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then treat with oil coming from the wound as long as it is healthy;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	and if the aphistma is the size of a vein, then you should take oil from your hand that you can get to the aphistma on all the skin, then remove the needle from its place where you hold it in your hand, and let it pierce, and it has two threads, so that you pull it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	then tighten the aphistma, as I told you, or the link of one of the two parts to the other with two threads;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	and if you doubt that the thread does not come out, then he will take another needle at all the threads from the incision of the first needle, and pull out the threads in four places;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then cut the abscess as much as the excess is released, then cut the excess with the curette and leave what is attached;
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then wrap him in a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil, then apply tent remedies and spices as long as he is healthy.
des apostemes des ners	of the abscesses of the kidneys
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	as they come out in the artery and in the vein, they come out in the kidneys when they are wounded, or through too much toil, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And if it happens more often with the shoulder joints and two legs or at all where there are joints, and this is a grieve abscess, and its color seems to be the color of the flesh, and many people are in pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when they are restrained so that the patient feels pain, and is not completely healed yet, but let the cure continue;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and does not move well in any way, and does not go forward or backward, nor up nor down, and what is in joints should not be cut with iron:
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	in case there is a contraction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and if it is at the head or at the forehead, make the skin with the sponge.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, and if he has a pimple, and copes it in its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, if the sore has hair, and skin it, then bone it and sew the wound up, and let it heal until it is well.
des grosses boces pendans	of the large bellies hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	No time has come when there is a wart in the belly or nowhere else, and it is a disease that is called "fungus" by appearance, and its root is fine, and its head is large;
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and of little and great moisture;
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw two homes where there were two warts that looked more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, they were white, and had a small root, and were split open, and ran with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I measured them and found one to weigh 18 ounces, and the other 6 Z. (possibly a unit of measure for weight), and the incisions so that you notice that the patient is moist, and the color of the arteriole is pale and moist and has a fine root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	If it is large with a wide spatula, and let the fire cautery be in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For when the tail comes out with great pain, and it leaves you, then hasten to cauterize;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	And if you see the patient in pain and frightened by the iron incision, then take a piece of string well made, and bind the arteriole as we have said, and let it be for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	and then restrain it, and do not cease to remove the string from the arteriole as long as it copes with the string, and move it a little by its own motion;
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	and if the roots are large, so be afraid of the coppers at once for the belly, but you put them well coppers half, then cautery that it does not come back;
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then heal the wound, and keep so you do not coppers the tangle which is of fuchs color and poor scent and milk regart.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess to which I will come in the treatment of the ulcer hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the breast is inflamed
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the boil comes by cautery of wound or cut of syphi, and is on the belly and there are some of the boils, as it happened in other ruptures, or of blood which cuts from veins or arteries according to what is before, or of windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is by the rupture of the syphi and by the issue of the boil, if the color of the abscess seems like the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and opening of different issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is by the outlet of the intestine, then there are many things, and when one presses it with his two hands, so that he repents, and then returns, and perhaps he is caught, and grows larger at the entrance to the bath and for great work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is because of moisture, it is a light thing, and open well when you press it to your hand, do not constrain it.
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	and if it is because of blood, let it open by these signs, the thick and hard abscess, and let it be placed according to a quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is because of windiness, if it is hot at the touch, and the opening if it is that you look at its appearance is for the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is appropriate that you leave the healing.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you, or chapister apomes, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if its appearance is for the intestine or loins, then it is necessary that you command the patient to tie his loins, and be stretched out straight, and then sign with your hand all around the loins;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then command him to walk slowly between your hands, then go into the place that you have signed all around the loins, then extend the half of the abscess from above to all the large nail;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	and then tie the foot with a strong thread or a strong silk rope tightly, and let us bind it up.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then operate on half of the appendix extending on the thread, and with your index finger press the intestine;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it stuck to the thread, then loosen it, and press the intestine towards the inside of the abdomen;
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the boil, take it with a blade, and cut off the surplus;
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or vein is against it, or if you have pricked it deeply, then go back to your work and take two needles, and thread them with two strong threads, and tie them up tightly where you made the hole that you made pierce;
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then stretch the appendix in four places on the needles, and if you see it, then remove the needles, and leave it there until it is rotten, and let the dead flesh drop off;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	Here is the translation of the first sentence: 
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And extract the blood where you see moisture, then treat the joint of what it touches, and weld the joint.
dou chancre	Dou Chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have spoken about the appearance of leprosy, and how one should act with medicine, and how one should avoid curing with iron.
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and let the leper go in the marris, and great care in the cure, and tell the old that when leprosy is in a limb or breast as leprosy is in meat, and in soup, and in similar foods, and it must all be cut off when it is in trouble;
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	and when he is large and old, so it does not come to me, for I never heal him;
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	no one ever heals before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And the shoulder, when it is in a limb where it can be cut off, as we have said, is that you do not purge any evil of black bile;
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	and then make him better if he has a manifest fullness, and then, made the patient comfortable to do the work;
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then put on them your scabs or sores, and the hair from all sides, and the bone from all sides without leaving anything;
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow freely, and compress the place well with your hand or with anything, and if the blood stops flowing, cauterize it until the skin is burned;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal him with other medicines as long as he is healthy.
de ydropisie	of droopsie
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have said in the division the appearances of dropsy, and in what way the gathering of the water is made, and the signs of each appearance, and the cure that is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron:
si est eclites soulement;	if it is only a fever;
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one must not touch iron in these two cases:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	this is to say, tympany and hypothermia, for it is a deadly thing;
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	so then when you treat this case of edema which is called "ecolthes" with medicines, and the cure does not benefit, if the patient is weak, or if he has another disease besides edema, such as flatulence and similar things;
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	if one does not touch iron, for there is doubt;
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	and if you see the patient of great vigor, and he has no other disease besides edema alone, and he is not too old or too young, then one must act thus:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	lay the patient down straight on your hands, and the assistant presses the abdomen at the lower part of the belly, then take the spatulum with thorns according to this shape:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	and be cut in two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	a point, and wherever it is not so deep that it might enter up to the intestine when it is put in, and not be able to be hurt.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	then see if there is dropsey [a medical condition where excess fluid collects in the abdomen] there above the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	if it is convenient that you cut them up from the back of the neck three fingers wide straight down on the breastbone;
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	and if dropsey [a medical condition where excess fluid collects in the abdomen] is there because of a liver disease, then your cut should be on the left side of the back three fingers wide straight down on the breastbone;
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	and if it is because of the wind, then it should be on the right side, and it is not convenient that the patient lie on his back on the cut so that the excesses do not run to the weak place;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and stretch it out, and hold your hand at the back of the neck from the skin to the spine as much as the length of an index finger or more;
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Then pierce the lozange until the spit comes out of its hole, and this is the place of the water, then the more it is hard, and it bottles this instrument from which thus is the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	It is like an elegant silver spike, and it is made of bronze or lightweight iron, and in its upper portion there is a small opening;
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and where it is bent on one side, there is an opening;
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and two on the other side, and one on the other;
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	and the head is cut off like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that the scribes cut the feather with:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	at the top of the instrument, so that when this instrument comes into contact with water, it drops immediately onto the instrument;
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	then make it half or a third full, because if you fill it more than that at the time, perhaps the patient will die from the loss of his spirit by the removal of his weapon, or he will faint, or come close to death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the disease and its hair mean;
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	then train the instrument and hold back the water, and it is held now by the curb that stops the hole that is above the wound, of which I have spoken, so that you pierce according to this manner;
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	then begin again with the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering from that, and train a small quantity of water;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	do not do this again for one day, and guard against making too much of it as long as there is no delay but a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you doubt about the patient, and you leave a little water for him, if his cure is in the earth or in the sand hot, and by sweating or bathing and in the sun, and if he gets tanned from drinking;
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and the treatment of desiccative medicines until he is well, and cauterizes on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after extraction of the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stop of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born with an imperforate penis, or if it is perforate, it is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary that it should be perforate at all, very subtle skin should be used according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	then put on him a thin cloth of linen, and tie it and hold it like this for III days or IV and when it begins to urinate, so take off the cloth, and let him urinate, and then put it back on;
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and by chance do not understand at all, because the urine that comes out strongly does not leave the cloth closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	The hole of the piercing is opened with medicine made from clove oil, as we have said, if it widens.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the pertus in their proper place are blistered, because no one is born who has the pertus at the top of the penis, so that he cannot urinate before he raises his penis up;
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and they cannot get pregnant because the material does not come out until it reaches the navel, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the way of the opening is that the patient lies down on his back, then the head of the penis and the cup are like the size of a quill, so that the piercing comes in the middle, as it should.
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful of the loss of blood that often comes, and if it happens, let the wound be staunched, and heal the wound until it is healthy.
des pustules de la verge	of the wart
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Often there comes an ugly scar on the penis, and it is a hideous sight;
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and of evil and good;
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	if you squeeze them with subtle strength, and wrap them and clean them all up, then put cotton wet with Egyptian ointment in a bandage;
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the wound with Diafinicon until it is healthy.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	If the wart is malignant, of a pale color and dripping, you must apply fire cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you have wrapped it up, and the scar is in the middle of the penis, and part of it is inside the skin and part outside, then remove the wrap that is inside first;
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	and when he is solid, if the doctor goes away.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you join it together, if not firmly secured, the joint of the penis may be pierced, and blackness and corruption comes to its penis and scrotum;
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	if it is necessary to cut off all that is black and corrupted, then bind on the plaster of honey and flour which is made from pomegranate skin and seeds, then cure with other remedies until it is healed;
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if blood flows from the injury, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	The cures should be combined in two ways:
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	For blood evaporation, and for corruption:
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the joint of the penis is corrupted and withdrawn, you must bind or lead the penis with a cord, and let the patient urinate;
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	and when the hair has grown out at the tip of the penis that has not yet been circumcised, or where there is an abscess or an ulcer, it is necessary that you scrape with a scraper instrument as long as the bonds are loosened, and the joint of the penis is freed from all sides;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	and if it is a painful thing to devise this, then you must scrape it with the spetumile of the root of the penis and the scrotum.
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	then cut deeply between them, and put a fine linen cloth wet in cold water on it immediately, so that it does not burn quickly.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	circumcision is not a dislocation of continuance if as other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	however when we perform this operation of our own will, and especially on children, it is necessary that we do the best work and the lightest work for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancient ones did not speak of circumcision for their children, because they do not use it in their law, and we have it only because we have acquired it by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have heard the greatest part of the masters and the most honorable who performed circumcision around the balls, and with force, and all a new thing;
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	If it is done with two threads, and by chance one of them breaks, then the skin may hang down and delay the work.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	Or the recovery of the cup, and it is doubled pain, and to the purification which is there from the hole is not assured the point of the member.
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and to the purification of the nail by accident escapes the wound, and corrects the work, and many times it comes up that there is no need for purification and I want it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the mouthwashing that is made so well on all the body of man I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, if you cut it evenly in L all parts stretch;
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but that the string be well tighten around the leather;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and the manner of the first work is that you make the child think, if he hears, that you do not tie the string too tightly around the stick, and then you make it rest in all ways that you can;
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	then make it lie straight between your hands, and resound the beats between your hands or shut your fingers so that the child does not see them, nor any of the tools;
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	and dip your hand to the root and blow on it, and tie it up high as long as the head of the root is;
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	Then wash it well with dirt that has gathered there, then tie the joint with a double thread, then tie it to the other one;
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	and hold it by the second thread to the thumb and to the index finger, and place between the two threads, then remove the cautery from above carefully and tie the head of the root;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	then let the blood flow little by little, because it is the bleeding;
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put powder on and on the powder I wrap with a piece of cooked egg yolk dried with rose water, mixed with good oil and fresh herbs, and let it sit for another day, and the healer treats it as long as he is well;
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The form of the cure for this disease is as follows:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The two bones should be soft and rounded, and the joints equal in length to each other.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	the mistake in the cure if it is when the curative fluid escapes from the incision;
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	then you must extend it to your fingernail so that the incisions form an abscess;
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and make it even, and if you cannot hold it with your nail, then hold it with pliers, and then make it even.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	If it lasts three days, and that which is sore at the root of the penis is swollen, if he leaves it until the abscess has dried up, and then scalds it lightly;
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	if you can move it as you please, and keep away from the part near the root of the penis, it will not harm you.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Cure also the powder that causes bleeding, which we have spoken of in our treatise on powders, and if applied too vigorously, it may cause injury to the upper part.
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore, as we have said, as long as he is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	retentence of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The holding back of urine is due to the extraction of stones from the urinary tract, or to frozen blood, or to bowels, or to a similar thing, which we have spoken of in our discussion of the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	and if the urine is not eliminated, and you see a stopping due to a stone in the urinary bladder or at the base of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be made to bend on his knees.
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	and let him put the stone on his back, and extend his abdomen from above his back, and restrain the patient so that he lies as flat as possible;
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and then forces the collar of the bladder to express itself on top of the stone, so that the urine is discharged;
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must bring the instrument called "syringe" to
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and be of fine light silver, like the feathers of an owl;
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and be of a long and half palm size, and be sharp at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the manner of the flow of urine is that you take a double thread, and tie it to the tip with a piece of wool or cotton, and insert the tip into the syringe;
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and fill the excess of the wool with oil or butter and linseed oil, and insert the tip into the syringe, then smear the syringe with oil or butter and linseed oil, and make the patient sit on a chair, and lubricate the bladder and the penis with moist oil of olive and water;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	Then hold the syringe lightly to the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then twist the penis over the bowl.
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	Then pour the syringe up to the bladder, and let the urine go into the empty thing, and it is not done in this order unless you are taking it away where it goes.
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then tie the thread to all of the wool piece by piece, and let the urine follow the wool, then remove it, and make the urine run.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and start the syringe again until the bladder is empty, and keep the patient calm.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When the scorbut or blisters come to the bladder, and it is assembled together, and you see it distilling water and medicine, if done with all the instrument that is called "clepsydra", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It's over, and if at third attempt:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	On one side, and on the other, as you see;
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	And the hair is cut so that the medicine does not stick well to the penis, if there is moisture, and it is pushed when necessary.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	and when you take your medicine out of the bladder, place the head of the cautery in the moisture, and treat with the treatment that follows.
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	if you pull the moisture onto the cautery, and then quickly twist the treatment that follows;
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	if the moisture enters in, and comes to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and this is the form of the subtle enema, from which one enemas the bladder:
si est ci:	if so:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	is made of silver or oak; and the shoulder is higher;
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and is tied to the breast or the neck;
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	then take a sheep bladder and put the moisture that you saw to prepare the enema into it, then tie it between the two breasts with a good double thread of string, and heat the bladder's moisture on the fire;
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	Then pour the wine in the chamber of the scrotum, then draw your hand over the bladder to all the moisture coming out, until the patient feels that this moisture has come to the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle on it, and pierce it roundly.
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	then pour in a strong liquid into these cavities, then assemble the circle as one assembles a tapestry, and put inside what you want of oil and moisture and water, and bind it in the instrument;
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and do so as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have said in the division of the ways of stone, and the extraction together with medicines;
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	and I said the difference between the stone within the body as rain, and all the signs, and in which stone one must work with a chisel;
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the penis.
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone that is lodged in the bladder often appears in children, and this is a sign that the fluid jumps from the bladder to the thin part of the kidney.
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and I cut off, and rub the patient's penis, and then wipe it many times, and then anoint it;
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and at the root of these movements, the foundation;
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and light is the healing of children until they are four years old, and great sorrow is in the elders, and at middle age is much trouble, to those who are between youth and old age;
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and the treatment of these who have a large stone is lighter than that of these who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, if it is necessary first to purify the patient with a hot bath, in order to draw out all the pus that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For he does not bother at any time to seek the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the feet and turn him upside down and move him so that the stone comes out of the bladder completely, and never cut from above;
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	and set him to sit between your hands unclothed, and his hands shall be on his thighs, so that the bladder hangs down all the way to his ankles;
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	then question and touch inside;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	if you feel the stone in the space, then hurry now to cut it off from the bone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not slip when touching all over, then wet your index finger with oil from your left hand, because the disease is incurable, or your right hand, because the disease is completed and accomplished.
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	and pour it down into its foundation, and question the stone, and when you feel it with your thumb, so that the urine comes out at the neck of the bladder;
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	then press on it with your thumb, and pour it out at the place where you see it cut off.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And command the minister to press the bladder toward his hand, and command him to extend his right hand up over the testicles, and his left hand underneath the skin that is above the testicles in the part where circumcision is made;
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	and then I pour the sputum by pouring, so this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And make a space between what is between the loins and the fundament, not in the middle but next to the left side of the womb;
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	and be right up against the stone, and your two be close to the fundament, and be the size of the stone, not too big;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	so that the press if what is between the loins, so that it does not work;
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and know that there is some stone where there are angles and edges:
si est griés a issir;	so it is cracked;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if there is some that is soft, like a ball, and round, whose exit is light:
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	So then where it has angles and edges, make the size bigger;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and if it does not jump, then you must extract it with pliers that are like a file on the head, so that the stone does not escape;
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	or you put a small, sharp instrument into the ear;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot do this thus, then let it be broken with a sharp instrument and if it is corroded, then extract it with vinegar;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	and if there is more than one stone, then first remove the largest one from the bladder neck, then cut it off, and the small ones after, if there are any more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	If the stone is large, it should be made into a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For two things happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	either he dies, or his urine comes out again because the head cannot close properly;
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but nevertheless you must try to extract it, or to break it with pliers, piece by piece;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	and when you have finished your work, employ the ointment of cinnamon and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and put on top of it a damp cloth dipped in oil and wine, or in oil and rosewater and cold water, to calm the abscess.
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	then wash the patient's neck, and do not remove the ligature until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you remove it, if the oil and water are very well separated, then the cure of the wound with astringent and balmy ointments until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if hot abscesses come into the wound and putrefactions of blood in the bladder, and hold back the urine, which is conveyed in some way so that it does not flow with the urine:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	then put some dry salt in the wound, and extract the blood, for if it remains, it will corrode the bladder and spill it out.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then raise the wound with water and sand and earth, and aid it in all ways that you can, until it is healthy;
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	and it is necessary that all the hours that you cure him, you bind his two legs, and gather the medicines on the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	If the stone is small, and he is taken out of the bladder with a stick and pushed in, and his urine cannot come out;
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	if the cure for this, that I have said above, that you cut it many times, is not sufficient to cure him, then you excuse the cutting because of this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have proven this.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take iron, forge it according to this form, and make it into three angulated pieces of iron rod.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	then take a thread and bind it around the root of the bladder so that it cannot come out;
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	then pour the urine into the bladder lightly, until it comes out to the stone;
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	and return the blade to your hand in the bladder little by little, until you can pierce the stone from another side;
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	if the urine comes out soon, then press your hand on him who is held back by the stone in his bladder.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	If it is immediately bruised, and jumped with urine, and is cursed the patient;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	And if you cannot do this for any reason that harms it, then I will file the stone and the other above, then cut the verge between the two lines, then extract it firmly, and clean the frozen blood which is in the wound;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healthy.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	It happened that a stone was stuck in the bladder of a woman, and if it ever happened, this is a painful cure, and is attacked by three things:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	one is that per adventure the woman is a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second is that we cannot find a woman who is able to disclose it to the mirages, even if she is married.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third way is that per adventure we cannot find a woman who is skilled in this art of hands;
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	and the fourth method is that the stone of the woman is more perfectly than the stone of the man, because it requires a deeper incision and there is great fear. And if this is necessary, you should call on a woman who knows well, and do not pull her hair, and if you do not pull her hair, do not ask for her to cut it;
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and the present a good ballade in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and commands her to do that which you command with respect to the extraction of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and look well whether this woman is a virgin;
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then it is necessary to put his finger or foundation and seek the stone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she pulls it out, she should hold her finger or hand firmly, and recommend to her that she puts her right hand on the bladder with her left hand.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	If she pees, then it is necessary that she move it from the bladder's entry to the anus, as far as it comes to the root of the thigh.
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then cut into the bone in the root of the thigh against the middle where it is moved apart, and feel the bone in that part;
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and do not move her back up the bone or anus, and make the cut first small;
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then pour the rain into the pelvis, if you feel the bone so close to the wound as much as the bone can come out, and know that there are many kinds of bones:
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	That is to say, small and large ones, sharp and smooth, long and round, and which have rained.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the appearance [of the stone], then you will know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if he does not come out, then put it in vinegar, and keep it for an hour as long as the stone is being strained;
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	and return to your work, as long as the stone is far away, and have the tools that I told you about for the extraction of the stone to help you in your work;
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	and if it goes out from you, and it is the artery that has been cut, then put the powder on the place and extract it little by little and by degrees, and do not repeat this, and leave the stone and do not draw it out, except by accident, so that the patient does not die;
puis cure la plaie.	and then heal the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the fire is gone from the wound, and the blood stands, if it returns to your work, as long as the stone is far away.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carnous
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	The water that is used for washing is nothing but a mixture of moisture or white wine, which helps to release the joints, which are contained in the egg;
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and is called "syfac", and is not properly in the shell of the egg, if one thinks that it is another egg;
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and this is the leather of the loins between the white syph that we have said;
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	if it does not come out.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this Ramie is so weak that it comes from the testicles, and this substance spreads.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And if this comes out with the percussion on the loins, and this moisture happens to many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	or is it declining to yellow, or is it without red, black, or white water, and this happens more;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs of conio-isthenic assemblage, for if it is or white that we have said, if it is the reons of an aposteme, I poc long as much as the figure of an O that does not open the loins, because it has moisture all around.
