Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes from the foundation itself, and is separated from the body, then it should be cut off or severed from the foundation, and this should be done.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres:	If you feel the tent, and there is within it the fabric or the shoulder or the thing that is about to pierce, if there is no way of comfort or hope except by the administration of one of the three ways:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	where you burn it as we have said, or you chop it just to the root, or if you cannot, try and treat it first as mentioned above.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not cut it too short, so that you do not chop the root of the hair, and come to the ends voluntarily;
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then treat it, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	if it is healthy again, or you remove the covering and clean it thoroughly after chopping off the root, or with a tent or some other tool;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then put on a new skin, as we have said;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement:	then study to restore the wound and to keep the fistula in the opposite part of the root:
si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	which is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere:	And never use this method for a fistula:
et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	and is when you put the tent into the fistula, and it is or it costs from the base of the delicate skin on top, so take a tent with a hole at the top according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I pour out water in two, and pour the tent into all the thread in the fistula as long as it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is leaking from the edge of the base inside, then remove the thread from that hole, so that you put your finger on the base;
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II;	and train the head of the thread, and join the two shoulders together, and hold them apart, and leave it for one day;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and do not restrain it at all, until the thread covers these joints that are between two, and they rub;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then treat the wound as long as it is soldered and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, if you make it pierce in all ways that you can, if it is not too perfectly enclosed.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not good to make the lacing shut too perfectly, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is well.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spike with thorns that one makes the fistula should be sharp, part and cut;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other hand no, so that you do not cover what you must not cover, as you see here:
des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	There are two ways of causing gangrene.
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	there are two ways of causing gangrene: either because they are deep in the foundation, like a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and if there is one or more, they are far from the foundation and at the top of the foundation;
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	but those that are far away if they have a little moisture, and then again or a little bit of clear water or a little bit of blood, and their color is like that of the flesh;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment for those who have them deep in the foundation is that you order the patient to sweat by sweating him in chambers until the foundations are far away, and the fils come out;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry, and hold it as with pliers, or if you hold it with your fingernail, then cut it at the roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if they cannot hold them back due to their moisture, take them from the sheet, or from the cotton, or from a piece of cloth.
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and pull them towards you, then wrap them up and powder them with any hot powders that are in the fire's place;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or fire cautery as it is said in the chapter of cauterizing, so that you cure them with other cures until they are healed;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if its foundation cannot come out, then cauterize the patient with a hot, sharp instrument to wash away what is in the foundation, so that it can come out freely;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	Can the patient be stretched out, and if his threads are firmly attached to the foundation, then the cure is light;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and hold them with your finger or pliers and wrap them up, then cure them as we have said until they are healed, and avoid cutting with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:	If it is necessary for you to add a suture in this way:
pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	Take a twisted thread and put it on a needle, then wind the thread around the needle and make the needle go through from the other side, and return the two ends of the thread onto the needle, and if it is wide;
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and tie the thread into a knot, then remove the needle, and do the same for all of them, and leave one there so that the blood may run out;
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put a damp cloth on the foundation with oil or balm, and put it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave it until it bleeds, and when it stops bleeding, if it is cured with ointment and other cures, until it is well.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	at the end or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Sometimes there is drying out at the end of the intestine, and by constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is not effective.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If it is necessary for you to rub the scab off with a spatula or your nail from above, which does not allow it to get wet;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	and then treat him as long as he is still alive as it should be.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if he cannot be sutured, then start shaving again more forcefully than before, until the wound heals and is scarred.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then treat him as long as he is still alive.
dou fremit	The patient should let the hair grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold them steady so they do not move until they grow.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Formica is a small appearance in front of the hole, and goes away completely.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and at no time does it hurt, and you feel it like death rumbles, and it comes all over the body, and more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the doctor must take a feather from an owl's wing, or a strong vulture's feather, and put that feather on the rumble until the purple circle covers the whole area.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand around all of the feather as you cover the entire area with it, and then fix it completely, and scorch the rumble from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, then make this of a dog's or a horse's or a pig's tooth according to this form, and be subtle and draw over it.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	Ne may percii, por muez tenee a doii, et muez preessee.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you feel pain, if the cauterization burns, as it is before or after the application of the cautery paste.
de la forme dou clistere	in the form of a clister
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	No matter if done with silver enema or oak bark, or with melted lead or moldy wine;
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	And no matter if these small or large instruments are used, according to the condition they are applied to.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	These therefore that one introduces in the cure of children and who are weak and painful, are little.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clister is little and big if it is above wide, or if the belly is tied according to this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	and I have observed a distension or an swelling, as you see, and a pain in the abdomen that pierces;
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	and there is a protrusion on one side of the abdomen, and on the other there is a depression;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and either the abdomen is drained with a bladder of beast or parchment, and piercing all around the little protrusions, and between each there is a space of thread, then tightly wrap the abdomen with a strong knot of thread crossed around it, and so gather the abdomen together as if it were a sheep;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	and when the medicine is inside, if the thread of the instrument in front of it is strong, then cauterize.
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	This is the shape of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	and let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head of the cauterizer with oil or olive oil or similar thing, then pour it lightly:
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	then the minister holds it with both hands until it is completely dry, then removes the cauterizer, and places the patient's legs against the wall, and lets the medicine come out, if necessary:
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he sleeps a whole night, then it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you bandage him with a plaster because of the decay of his belly, and the medicine comes out quickly, then wait until he is well.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament or abscess, then let the cauterizer be as subtle as for a child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	This is the shape of a thin cauterizer above where the skin is stretched:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have said above in the division the treatment of wounds;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	Or we will tell you the cures for hands and medicine, according to compleness.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various according to what they are made, and according to the places or wounds they are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things that cause wounds are by hitting with a stone, or cutting with an épée or a couteau, or a lance or a fust or a saiette, or similar objects;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or that are made according to the laws of the corps, such as a wound that strikes the neck, or the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, for the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, if it is by hitting with a stone or similar things, and the skin is all torn and the wound is great, and you doubt much about the apotheosis:
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	If he comes soon enough to the head, if there is no blood from the wound, and if it is applied in the opposite direction of the wounded part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and abstain the patient from wine and fattening meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	If he does not heal soon, if his flesh is wasting away, and if he does not drink wine or eat cheese;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, if an abscess forms, wet it with oil and apply a hot poultice or wine that stifles;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no heat on the wound, if it is fresh and not moved by the wind, dust; I will say a little later:
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if fire has moved it, if he puts on some onions, until he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great as of a sword-slayer and like it, and the lips cannot be brought together by tenderness, if they are brought together by sewing, as I say to the wounds of the belly, by the seam.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is open to the bone and dry, and holds only a little blood, then
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And then heal the wound with medicine, and restore it with hard skin in place of leather, and instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as roasted testicles and bread, and also poultry and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find leather rot, and it doesn't reach the bone, then cut off the rot completely, and burn it, then heal it;
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or a vein, from which blood cannot be stopped by medicine, then cut the artery, and if you find it dislocated, then let it return to its place like a thread;
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if that doesn't help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the light healing is:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	Here is that you put in this powder which hardens so that fire moves it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the way of the powder is thus:
pren encens une partie;	Take incense a part;
sanc de dragon II parties;	dragon's blood two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	chald the live three parts, and the powder slightly, and employ the wound, and holds it firmly, until it is well healed and joined to all its dragon's blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then bind it well, and leave it undisturbed, if it swells;
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for the medicine should not be removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never do we use this clay alone, except that incense or dragon' s blood is not moved, but that fire has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the fire has moved the wound, even slightly, put at least half of this powder on it;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some olive oil or grain flour made from water and honey, until it is well cooked;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then he should cure with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the fracture of a bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it gently with tweezers;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you here the breaks of the skull.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	For if the wound is in the throat, and it is simple, then there is no difference between it and that of the head, but it hurts at the throat where the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is a baby, if there is no other device than to let the cure take place and not put anything restricting, because it hurts the baby and makes it retract;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything on the wound, for the substance of the baby is cold and its circulation is with the brain, which is the highest member;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but be the medicine soft, as hot water in lukewarm water, and mixed with oil of roses, and wash it too with lukewarm water, and other stones of minimal value according to this way, and moistened with oils.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, so that the scar is long, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and he is shaved and full of hair, then pierce or cut lower down;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery has been cut and bleeding occurs, then stop the flow of blood, and cauterize it as well;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	and if the throat is cut, or the voice, and the course is maintained, so that the meat goes down, if the voice is cut on the neck of the throat, and does not touch the throat but is put back in its natural form;
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then hold it in place and let it rest for a few days, and then treat with onions until he is well;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, let it be probed;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if there are pieces of bone, if they can be taken out whole, and those that cannot be taken out whole, leave it until the wound festers and drains, and let the discharge come out and the wound be cleaned;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on the powder I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and it has developed an abscess, then treat it as I have said in my chapter on abscesses.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a lance or dagger cut, and the wound is deep, look at the wound from all sides and massage the patient's flesh:
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If the wound is mortal, then
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	If the wound is not profound and is fresh with blood, then put the powder to it immediately so that it does not hold back the blood, and let it rest in the body, and close the wound.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	However, I do not advise applying a poultice today and tomorrow, but rather leave it uncovered.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	If you do not have an ointment, then put a wet cloth on the wound to absorb the moisture and let the patient lie down on the wound for three days, or four, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	If there is no spasm, nor a painful trembling of the body or extraction of an alien object;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	Then, when you see that the bones are in place, know that the wound has been saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal this wound with the medicine of tent and other medicines, until it is well;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal, then know that there is a fistula.
si la cure si com on doit.	if the cure is as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is caused by a blade or knife and is straightforward, or in the back, or at the top, then know the cure of that which is before.
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	if it is large, from sewing;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, from powder, and if it has broken into the bone, and has come loose in pieces, then know the wound, and the dangerous parts if they are separated;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not separated, then leave the wound to fester, and then extract with care;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds and other limbs, this is the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Dou derrompement dou ventre
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The breaking open of the belly is great and wide and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	From the great wound, let there come none of the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, so that the entrance of the bile does not happen.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the stitch is more painful, and there comes no small wound than the great one, so that it is not better to put the intestines back in, if they are not put back in from warm to warm;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	because the intestines swell so that they feel cold, if they are put back in, and because it is better to leave the small wound alone, because if you leave the intestine at its place than at the others II.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to IV manners:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	the common stitches have in the stitch of the belly, and the stitch of the other wounds of the body and two other proper stitches are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and nevertheless they are more proper with the stitch of the belly, and I will say each one and will declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and there is no matter of the intestines outside, and there is nothing to put back in it, this is done by one of two ways.
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen with fever.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, heat it in the third way:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	moisten a sponge or I mool dried cloth in cold water only, or you cook in hot water and cumin and spice, and rinse the intestines until they swell;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and never do this while restringing, and be wet that you are cool by dislodging it.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling go away, if you moisten the intestines with cold or hot water and cook them, because this keeps the entrance closed to little things;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if he cannot enter, then make a little cut in the wound with the instrument with which we cut the hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first cure is to put it to bed so that we do not have to chop it off unless there is great necessity;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	this is the instrument with which one divides it;
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut into the core and then pull it out and form it like this:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines protrude, if you return them to their natural place in their proper position, if you can do so, for that is necessary.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide and in the lower part of the abdomen, then you must make the patient lie on their back, and put their legs higher than their head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if the wound is in the lower part of the abdomen, then put the head and breast higher than the lower parts, and so the opening of the abdomen is in one of the two parts, so that you align it with the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and so it is necessary to treat what I have said here, in great wounds and small ones.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	In small wounds, however, if you are unarmed, then place your hands over the wound and bind it with a cloth that covers the whole tear to your hand, and join the lips together;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and that is the common way of stitching, and it is that you should squeeze a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave some space from the top of the wound, and put in a needle with very strong thread;
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two ends of the leather with the two ends of the thong, which is inside the leather, until you make it piercing from that side, and join the two ends of the thong together, all four together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	then remove a double thread from the needle from two sides, then join the two ends of the wound together, and then leave some space, and put in another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	and then lay it on thread as you did the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to what you need with needles until all the wound is closed;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and let the needles be fine and coarse, because the fine needles go through all the cloth, and the very coarse ones cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for it is necessary that they are small;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and do not put the needles too far away from the edge of the cloth and hide, so that they go through and open the wound before it is healed;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then cut off the heads of the needles so that they do not hurt the patient when he sleeps, and put a blanket or sheet over the heads of the needles to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this way of sewing with needles is more convenient for small wounds, because it requires only one needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second stitch is common, and it is that you join the two pieces of leather with the two pieces of thread together on an awl or there is one strong line of thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have pierced these three together, I will take the awl to the part where you began, in the way that we sew clothes.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put space between each stitch the thickness of a small nail;
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This stitch is good for a man, and I will sew up an injury that he had or his belly, which was torn by a knife, and the wound was more than two palms in length, and there were intestines about two palms in length, and the wound went into his belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought him back his intestine when he had been out for 22 hours, and the wound was sewn up after 15 days, and I treated it, and he was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the miraculously happened that he died, and this is a wonder;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not cure him with ointment, for I was in a place where there was no ointment, nor any medicines;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and dip it twice a day in the wound, and wash it with honey water until it was well.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	I will now tell you the two proper ways to stitch:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and pass it through the flesh from outside in;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	When it has pierced the flesh from right to left, so that the thread or stitch goes through the flesh, and you have threaded the needle, and pierce it from the other side from inside out;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and know about this stitch that you also sew as the pelters do fur, and let the fur be on one side, and take it up on the other, until the stitch is finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second way to stitch, which Galen properly describes, so that as if no one were sewing it, putting together the two parts naturally, and applying one of the heads where the stitch goes to the other head in this way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Place a pin or spike near the mirror above, and pierce that single point alone, and leave the two shoulders in peace.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	Then turn the needle, and pierce it from the outside part only up to the middle point of the two shoulders.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then pierce one and then the other from the outside part only up to the middle point of the two shoulders, in the two other shoulders that are on the other side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the method of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galien thus says in response to that statement, and no one contradicts him: when sewing the belly on two needles, each with its own thread.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And one needle must be pushed from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew with needles for corroding.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and know that when the breach is in the middle of the belly, then the stitch is greater than those on either side of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgments for the wound are such as they are for other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, so that the arrow has moved it, if you put back the intestine and the stitch;
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and then put on the powder that rubs in, and if the arrow has moved it, put on any ointment that is present, until the wound dries up;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cook the thread, and let the sutures be tight, and the wax;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the wound as with others, until it is healthy;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you have no medicine, put on, soon enough that it begins to dry up, cotton wool, and stir it twice a day until it is healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you have no other need for medicine in many cases when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you doubt that the wound does not make a union with the principal members, then it is appropriate to moisten another light in oil of thyme or oil of roses, and place it around the joints, and cut off the tendons;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if it hurts or puts on a rash in the bulges, and many times comes, if the blisters of black wine are washed off, and most often the putrefaction comes up to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierces it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is lighter to be healed than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jeun" cannot heal when it is still attached to the womb, and this is because of the formation of veins, and the subtlety of all the body, and its nearness to children.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the scar jumps out of the wound, it is reset backwards as well as the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it is old and becomes blue or black, it is appropriate to lay the site that is black, so that blood does not come, for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and wrap what is between the bandage, and place the two shoulders hanging from the edge of the wound to the end so that the extraction when the bones chitter, and the wound oozes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestines are torn, and the wound is small, then can one restore it in some men, for I have seen that some were pierced by a bow or an arrow from a lance's belly;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it oozed and became a fistula, and there was vomiting and wind;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated him according to what I could do, and did not cease to subdue it until he was healed, and his bones were mended.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw the man mended, I doubted that the disease had not done him harm in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no evil, but delay in better conditions, and eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and say no experiments that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied in some way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take three fingers from a big testicle, then join the lips of the wound, and when the fingers have opened the mouth, put it on the two lips, so that she draws her mouth out;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then he covers the head, and this remains in place so that it cannot be separated, then he puts another finger after in the same way as before, until the wound is completely covered;
et cout la plaie.	and cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	This chief if it burns in the intestine, and causes no harm to the patient, and can be tied with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal in some way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	take the end of this thread of intestine that has been carefully cut off, and then tie the end of this thread to the end of a thin twisted linen thread, then tie the thread to the needle, and in cutting the intestine, and take it back out of the incision;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this method of suturing frissons is good only according to the way of faith and hope.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, most importantly when it is in one of the internal groins, there is no cure except by carefulness.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	from fistula or which it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that all wound or abscess, when it heals, is called "fistula" in general, and most so when it is scarred and turns into a bowl.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to the true notion wrong and white, where one does not feel pain, and it is also like the feathers of an owl;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and never clearly in a clear bow, and sometimes thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	and never pokes, and sometimes is enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	I have already spoken in the division of wounds that any wound that is not healed and there is no cure, it is good only by one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the little of the blood or the color;
ou por sa malice;	for his evil.
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	with a sharp edge within, and on the lips, so that it does not grow there;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or where there is too much bowels;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	whose skin is rotten, and the substance is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or whose medicine is not good for the cure;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or where the corruption is like that of a pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or whose property in the region is late digestion and late health, and goes away by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already explained all these causes and signs, and the remedies of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or covient that I do make you know the cure of fistula which is made by oevre of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	I know that a fistula can occur in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the sinews, or to the spine of the back, or to any of the joints of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if so that comes to the principle member's property, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are in this way are of great sickness, and there is only toil, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is no fistula that does not come to the level I have said, and you have promised to heal it, and you see it clearly, so take a tent of rain or iron, if the fistula is straight, so ask it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is twisted, then seek it with a thin tent of vinegar, for the vinegar bends slightly within the curvature;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the fistula is very broken and you cannot properly seek it with tents, then let it be cleansed with vinegar through one of the breaks, for it moistens so much from one break to another, and purifies;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and then examine the swelling at your hand, that you know if there are any bones or nerves, and it is completely shaved off, and ask the patient very well about the pain that he feels when you squeeze his hand, and the place where he feels it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, whether it is good or bad, cut off the false joint and the corrupt joints that are within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then cure it as long as it is healthy, and the fistula is very deep from the right place, so that you cut it perfectly well as much as you can, then you put wet medicine on it until the chief of the fistula, so that the medicine corrupts the excess that has been kept at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I meet ointments healing the disease, as long as it is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	If it is not healed with this, then let him be cauterized as we have said, and if his bone is corrupted by the abscess, let him take care.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve is injured in the main members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if his bone is exposed and there is corruption and darkness, let him treat it with healing ointments as long as it is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if it is not healed, and its bone returns to its place as before, know that you have not gone far enough in the treatment:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	if it is exposed and kept until you are at the bottom, and all the bone corruption is removed, then restore the joint;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is healed in this way, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that corruption is too perfect, so you cannot come.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy than to let nature take its course;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is one small bone corrupted, and you can pull it out with tweezers, if there are many bones, pull them out one by one, leaving none behind;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if the moisture causes opposition and it is hot and humid, and copious moisture and sweat, deliver the bones;
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, put on the wound something that promotes corruption, and leave it there for a while until the bone is腐敗したのです。
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	then if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, put on the wound a black substance until all the bone has腐敗したのです。
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of the wound腐rot, and comes up to just short of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it is properly sewn and covered all the way to the corruption, and then treated as long as it remains solid;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And I will tell you about a hunchback who happened to him in his leg, so that you take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	He was a young man of about 30 years old, who had a pain in his leg from an inner cause, so that the matter came out to the leg, and there was a large abscess, and he had no reason for opening it.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	But the mirror, due to his madness, opened it so much that it corroded a lot of matter, and became a fistula, and came to be very dangerous, so that everyone was afraid, and there was moisture and moisture in the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many times I have cured them in two years, and there was no skill in the art of hands until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines that were used to cure him, and those that run through the large passages with great pain;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and became red in the youth's body, and had an orange color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I fixed a tent in one of those holes, and then searched all the holes, and I found that one came out against the other on all sides of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	So I hurried then, and копал in one of the passages as far as I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotted and broken, and the corruption came to the bone itself;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I knew what had been taken from the bone, and I took care that there should be no other corruption than that which I had taken out;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with medicines that are used by long time, and could not hold it together;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I began, and uncovered the bone as before, and found continued corruption in the bone, and burned it, and then put the bone back together, and bent over to weld the joint;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not so much as cup my hand around one end of the bone, and I took it away from all its ends, then I restored it with medicine;
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and he was healed and firmly welded together, and it would no longer be necessary to open the wound for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Car for the evacuation of blood there was often, but he was healed entirely, and gave birth in place of the bone a hard child, and was of good temper and did not have any harm or opposite from all in all, nor air nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the skeleton, then it should be treated in this way:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	take a stick, and extend it at the top of the bone which is separated, and
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and put another thinner line of thread on the other side of the bone, and tie it above the separated part, and let the thread extend to the end of the bone, and then take off the thread from the top of the bone, and uncover the thread where you see that it should be tied, so that the thread does not fray the bone;
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a stone or a wedge of wood under it to move the chest;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and wait until one can see and feel the corruption, and another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the whole chest;
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then put a wedge under it, and then unpick the corruption from one part to another, and pick the wound long where the corruption is; as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cover the joint with corruption, and unpick the bone where it is;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other angle but to cover it;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if the corruption is at the base of the hand, or at the base of the foot, then this is a very bad thing, but you must first inquire about that corruption, how it hurts you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and clean in all ways that you can, but that the vein or nerve does not make you contrary;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the incisor and the saws for covering these bones are many, according to the siteness of the bones and the appearance of the teeth, and their largeness and their finenesse, and their height and their smallness, and their hardness;

et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manner of the diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if he thinks the instrument in which you are skilled is suitable for him.
dou feu	fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head may be dislocated by a fall or by being pushed out of place;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have medicated this corruption by the cure of medicines, and it does not profit, if you cover that member to the place where the corruption comes, so that the patient escapes from death by the corruption of the member itself, or by the malice, which is greater, of the loss of the member;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the signs are that the limbs become black, if it seems that they have been burned by fire, and after that darkness, for corruption of the member from member takes place, and embraces all the body.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if it is due to copper, and if it is caused by the stinging of certain poisonous animals, such as sea scorpions or weasels, then the corruption is at the top of the two bones, if it cracks, and give it no space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes only up to the hand, if the crack is at the joint, so that the corruption does not come up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	And if it comes up to the arm, if the crack is in the shoulder;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the shoulder, then it is death, and there is no remedy except to take all of its virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and until the rust comes where the stone:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it comes in the first joint, then the cap after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes where the stone, then the cap all the way down;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises up the leg, then the cap at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other danger to the patient but death;

Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if the pain comes when you work, then cauterize the area thoroughly, or put some powders that restrain it on.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your medicine as long as it is complete, then tie the injured member with a convenient bandage, and cure it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	And I will tell you what happened to him at home in some detail:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	He had a blackness that seemed like fire, and this corruption came first to his foot, staining the entire foot;

Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	No time comes when the abscess is in its place, and delays so long that it makes a great assembly of bowels;

Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	If you have cooked the meat and it is still partially raw, and the meat is thin like a blanket, then you should cook it in a bath.

Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bow is complete, if it does not leave a gap.

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the toe of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Pancreatic is an abscess that may emerge from the nail of the hand, or of the foot, or perhaps may emerge in another two;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it has broken open, and no attention is given, then it may come to the formation of an abscess, and corruption and pus fill up so much at the root of the nail that perhaps it may fill them all up;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes the corrosion just to the bone, as much as there is stinking pain, and the shoulder of the two wide bones, and the color flows.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not take, then you must take away all the surplus that has been stored up under the finger nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The caustic is a great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the nail presses the wound and pricks it, and bleeds it, then you should put a hot and corrosive remedy on it to cut off all of it;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then he cures with onions as long as it is healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it and trim it, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see the two corrupted, then cut them off as much as it is healthy;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is wild, and gurgling, and smells of great pain, then you must first heal it.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	then cut the nail down from above with a chisel at an angle, and be careful that the cutting does not reach the bed of the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if there is something on it that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	la douleur du cœur de la main
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	Les deux membres qui naissent dans les mains de certains hommes sont parfois charnus, et parfois osseux, et n'ont jamais d'ongles, et aucune racine de la jointure ne nait en aucun d'eux.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Whoever is born in the middle of the neck does not move, and whoever is born at the hinge joint may move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The size of that which is chubby should be small:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it in its root with a large chisel.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	Whoever is born at the hinge joint should be treated with great care:
si te tien dou coper.	If you keep it covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In those who are born in the heart of the joint, if it is right that you cut the rounded part up to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable thread, and then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The dislocations that come together by nature at birth, or by the assembly of a wound, or by fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If you believe that you can cover the one that is withering, so that it repairs itself according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between two blankets or sheets wet with oil so that they do not stick together.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or put between two thin rags so that the threads do not stick together, as is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	Se soudemens comes to any of its two with the palm, so hold it firm as it should be.
des vils	of
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The veins are grossly wrapped with excessive melancholy matter, which comes from many members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more comes in the legs of those who go on foot and work and carry, so that others
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore you must not at any time administer a laxative to him, but cure him from the base.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The cure with iron is done according to two methods:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is that they are boiled, and the black blood is drained;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and another way is that you open the vein and drain it all.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The size should be determined according to this method:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	first make the leg hot with strong water until the thick blood is thinned, then draw the leg of the patient from above the thigh down to the ankle;
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	and cut the vein in I place, or II or III, of large size, then slice and draw strongly out black blood to your hand, from one top to another, as much as much of blood the virtue of disease can bear;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bandage it, and command that he turns his meat with black pepper;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and start again the evacuation and the bloodletting when veins are clear, and press on the disease.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The healing is done according to this method:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Reheals the leg of the disease: if there is hair, then he puts it in water, and bathes it with hot water until it turns red, and opens veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you don't have a bath, heat it over fire, and then cut the vein at the top of the shin, or in the part below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	and soak the skin with vinegar, and scald each side until it feels hot;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and when it is red and black, and when it enters or leather so seems as a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then pour the wine into it until it is warmed by the leather, and then dip it lightly in vinegar, and then cover it with a cloth for three days;
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then scald the skin on the vein until it feels hot, then dip it lightly in vinegar, as you have done, and then cover it with another knife, as you have done first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then cut another size, or more if you need it, then dip it and then cut at the second level, and then treat and dip again;
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then extract from one size to another until it has completely dried up, then cut off;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and if you can't pull and lift it out, then put a needle on one of the threads, and tie it up and pull it out, and cut off the thread, and turn your hand back and forth until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and keep it from slipping, because if it slips, then you can't pull or lift it out, and this causes harm to the patient.
