et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have finished treating it, put wet wool soaked in wine and oil on top of the wound;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until he gets better.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if it is twisted and bent and wrapped up together, and it isn't straightened out, as we have said, then you must cut it open, but don't cover it up;
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and pull it apart as we have described before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron where the thread slips should be curved, and don' t cut it off, so that it doesn' t slip into the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is a large loop, because if it were thin, it would wrap around the vein, but it is thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein runs through the legs, in warm places where there are no herbs or trees, and on the ground where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	And perhaps it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this causes the skin to peel off from within, as if it were crawling and winding between the leather and the skin.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this wound are that there is a very great swelling in the leg, then the shape of it changes, and the wound begins to come out, just as the root of a plant does.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the head is open, if you wrap a piece of cloth around the head from one and a half feet to two feet long, and then cover it with the cloth, and leave the cloth hanging down the leg, and whenever there is no more cloth on the leg, if the cloth is wrapped around the head again, and covered.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, take a part of it, and wrap up the rest, and do not cover it at all in its root as long as it is all out;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you take it, so it enters the chest, and brings an abscess and corruption to it or there, and causes a bad disease;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	for this thing, it is necessary that it be treated little by little up to the chest, and nothing remains of it or there;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and this vein does not come out when it is treated with the palm of the hand or ten fingers, and a great many come to me, to which she was of ten fingers long, and when you take it, if it bottles or breaks, and pierces up to the fundament, so that all comes out;
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and the material that is inside be empty, and bring to its place medicines against corruption every day, then heal it as you would treat an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And in no way shall hands be held to this vein, and least of all when it opens in the joint of the foot, or the foot itself, for it is a great risk, and from which rain comes.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 Cure therefore as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers which are born between leather and horse
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called in our language "buff disease", because it often occurs in buffaloes, and is a small worm that arises between skin and carriage, and goes up and down all over the body, causing burning as it moves from one member to another, until it comes out of the skin, and then it jumps away;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And is infected with pus caused by certain humors, so that they come towards, spiral, and shine, and are like worms or maggots in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	And there is doubt of its maliciousness, for when it goes through the body, and comes to the head, and enters the oil, by chance it returns, and destroys the oil;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it治it and extractit, then can't one do but once:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	So then it is necessary that you place the head up and fixit with a strong knot tightly, then push down and treatit firmly, and let it move freely in the socket, and if you don't findit, then cauterizeit with fire while it's moving:
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does, is if it tears the oil, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the oil, then extractit it carefully, then push down and treatit firmly:
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and use the medicine of washing with soluble medicines to remove bad humors from rot, and wash himself with meat that is rotting:
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some limbs, and moves from limb to limb;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I saw what I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arms, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and I poked after, and I saw it rise as quickly as a worm does, as if it were silver, when it cuts from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain departed from that place, and it entered into her shoulder, and then a poking after came all through the body, until it came to her other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	and then she told me that she was twisting all through her body again, as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled how she moved from member to member, because I had never seen this disease move in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Anyway, many had wanted to move their pain from one place to another, but I did not want to do so, as I saw it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought that this was why the woman's body was so cold, and her veins uncovered, and because her breath appeared to be constricted;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and do not agree with this treatment for those who are very hungry, and have moist bodies and closed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you treat this disease and the patient feels that pain, if it does not open as we have said, put a bandage on it and bind it tightly, and then cut it off as much as it hurts;
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the wound;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see your hair, take care of those who cause the wind to blow out, as if they were foul pills, and pills of serapin, and similar things.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	are various, according to their appearances and according to the places of their entry into the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that there are those who have long points, short points, hair, and welded;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those who have two angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and that moves in any member in two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	If a member is principal, as the skull, heart, liver, stomach, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When she falls off in any of these parts, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, you
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	it is appropriate for you to wash out this arrow, because death comes after many preparations;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when the bad sign does not appear to you yet, and the arrow is not fully extracted, if you pull it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the skull when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and the fluid that comes out which is on the skull, is when there is a scabies and sweating and twitching and redness in them, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and convulsions and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of food;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and maybe it will come out of the nostrils or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it will come out with speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and jumps out of the moist sore looking like pus, and in such a way that it seems to burn as fire;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and this sign reveals itself, if you have the cure, and extract the arrow if it is embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it hurts or rubs, is that it is near the left breast, and also seems to be pushed into something hard, not into a hollow thing;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the arrow also becomes pus, and in white color, and comes cold and cold sweat, and faints:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then you must know that death draws near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of the snot when it comes out is that without a plume of foam jumps out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's color changes, and he gazes upward and shivers with cold.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow has entered into the covering of the thigh, take care of the small bones;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and get great weakness and great pain and sighs;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and they move all the limbs of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the snot comes out in the stomach, perhaps some meat is vomited up.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow is lodged in the belly, and it does not come out through the intestine, then there is no hope for the cure or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if an arrow is embedded in the bladder, and urine flows out and runs away, and the patient feels great pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	it means that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, if as with the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the ajutoire and the spine and the force and the cul and the legs, and the limb that seems to be affected, are safe according to many dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or an artery, and it does not come out, then as I will tell you what happened to me, do the opposite.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	There was a man who had an arrow embedded in his neck or throat at the root of his throat:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it and dislodged the arrow from one side of the ear fat, and was healed without sensation.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And he dislodged an arrow from one side of the oil fat with a stick, and the arrow was reinserted, and only the point poked him in the back, and the arrow was a great green color, and weighed down his ears;
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The game was healed, and no other accidents happened to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I saw an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic at the ears.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I saw the hair, and made it grow long, and healed the Christian.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I saw an arrow in his chest or stomach, and I thought he was dying;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then that he passed thirty days, but his condition did not improve;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut up the arrow, and removed it, and I drew it out, and he had no bad effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if there is a Christian who has an arrow in his butt or back, and the wound is closed;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and let the arrow stay inside him, and do not change his natural dispositions, nor find harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man, to whom an arrow fell into his face, and the wound was closed;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and it delays so much suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many others' appearances.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And there was a bolt to the king of the Prince, that was him in the middle neck, and was slightly inclined on the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the bolt was all bent.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to heal after that she had been lame for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound to be very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I asked her to try all sorts of remedies, and I did not feel it;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pain and injury in his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the bolt of the king I put on the leech and the digestive tar, so that his legs did not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the bolts.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I put on the leech after three days, and resolved the wound quickly, and so much suffering lasted for a long time, until he felt the bolt inside his neck;
et il le me dist.	and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I put the corrosive herbal medicine on the wound for as long as it was open, and tested it, and felt the head of the arrow in its place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I tightened the opening of the wound with that herbal medicine, until the head of the arrow was clearly visible;
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and I left it for three months, and then I opened the wound again, and the scar was so large that I had to use pliers on one side and pull, but I couldn't get it out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	then I stopped trying to use subtle and ingenious ways to get tools, until one day I got a pair of pliers, made according to the shape that will result from this chapter at the end, so I opened it, and put the wound back together.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And I see that the cartilage at the nose cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I reset it then, and it was sewn up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Or you told me the quality of extracting certain arrows, so that you put your treatment on those that I did not say, because the book cannot include everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	But the master doctors compare very little thing well, and on those that are present and failing, they have nine operations and nine instruments for dealing with strange things that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that the arrows should not be from the limbs except as per two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either at the entrance where they enter, or from another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and those that go out by way in which they enter, are arrowheads penetrating into the flesh, and should never stay stuck now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if she does not jump now, let her wait until the hocks are rotten inside, and let the birth come.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if she is stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, let her wait a few days, and let her mud each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then she jumps, and if she does not jump, let him open all the small veins inside very well, until the blood flows inside, and then tie it up.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes down to one of the groins of the skull, and any of the accidents that I have said open up the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	if you don't pull it out now, but let her be even for a few days, because if the arrow comes to the sinuses, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not lodged in the bone but comes only up to the sinus, and the patient remains for a few days without any bad accidents, then the device for removing it can be used.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if she is very stuck inside and cannot come out, if he gives her bloodletting inside, as I told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then heal the wound as long as it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is reinserted in the neck so that it cannot be seen, and you want to find it with all your strength;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, and then take it with any suitable tool;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot take it out by pressure on the wound, and because of the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then break it as much as the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and if you can take the arrow out, and if it has ears to hold it in place, then remove or bend the arrow until you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully so that you do not break the arrow, and then draw it out more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot pull once, if the hair until the base is rotten, then try, for extraction it is difficult.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if this remedy of blood makes the patient contrary, then administer what we have said about the treatment with his ointment.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and be careful of the incision of the nerve and the vein, and do not try to extract the arrow without danger, soon or slowly, or firmly or loudly;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and set the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow entered, for this is the greatest help that can be given, and if you cannot do so, then follow what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another direction, and does not open anything of the body, or if the skin is swollen in a certain place, so that it can be seen or felt:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	Cut him down, as far as the hooks can reach, and then extract them:
si saut fuer maintenant.	if it were now
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand roundly until it enters into the bone and widens the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be extracted, then leave it for now, and then begin the extraction again as soon as it comes out:
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is an arrow, put it to the whole shaft.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if there is a splinter, and you have a file, if you file the end of the splinter so that it enters into the channel of the tool;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then pour on, and if the arrow is filed, pour the file onto the end that enters, so that the extraction may be easier.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is lodged, then it is necessary that you cut all around the place where the arrow enters; if you can, do so, and then treat the wound as it is necessary to do.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	and if the arrow has entered or is in the chest or bladder or side, and it is near, and you can cover it, you can cover it.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and keep yourself from covering the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound, for that is a job.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is well.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the pliers that are used to treat arrows are similar to an eye, and thus the shape is this:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	great, middle-sized, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the butt-end is also like the beak of a bird, to fit to the tip of the arrow, as this is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The pliers for fitting and for picking up are these.
des voinnes dou cors communes	Veins from the chest
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	Of the veins from which one heals are XXXI; of which there is head XVI.
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	The two bats that are behind the ears, which are called "dous herbech";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in two temples appearing;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in two limbs of two eyes, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is at the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the head from the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugular veins that are at the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth, which are called "augeherich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are behind the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	Of the veins from which one commonly heals are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cerebral, and is on the left side of the neck, and it is called by lay people "voine du chief";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the name is called "fasting", and is composed of the cephalic and basilar, and they call it "vein curer";
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilar is on the right side, and they call it  "vein curer", and is on the top, and this one which is said, who opens clearly on the navel.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the little finger is the vein that is between the index and the ring finger, and if it has II rains;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and where the foot are III veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is located on the back of the hand on the left side, and the second one that is at the ankle on the right side;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein that is called "nerve", which is in the ankle on the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are III veins of those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The ear drains after the ears that help the old catarrh, and causes migraine.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the quality of the ear drain, as I told you, is that you remove the head of the sick person and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	and then tie the patient's neck with a rope so that the two veins appear behind the ears attached to the head;
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then place them on your right side, and where you feel the pulse of your right side, sign with your hand;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lance and pierce through the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand up to all the vein in front, and cut it and the skin and the vein very well on both sides, and make the blood flow until you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then extract and bandage it, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The two arteries that are in the two temples, if they are of an old age, and سودة, and a customed ophthalmia, and at the base of the tears, to the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the surgeon is so as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	that the patient draws his chin back until the two veins are clearly visible;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse at the base of the tongue, and then sign with the index finger;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then put the knife on the vein at the top of your second finger, and cut it, and then cover the vein, so as you have done with the two veins before, and make the blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then wash the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then make a cast, and leave it until it is healed;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have spoken about their operation and extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of a frontal vein is as effective as the treatment for an ancient facial disease, and causes migraines and dizziness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that the patient twists his neck until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument which is called "a pit-drill", whose form is this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and hold it with your hand, or with another thing, and let blood come according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then remove the neck from the patient, and tie the vein until it is healed, and do not work a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, it is not fitting for the flames to be too hot;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and the bone is close by, for the bone may break if the flames are too sharp; and the fire may die out when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The two veins that are in the two arms should be treated with hair, and for scrofula, and jaundice, and eye diseases, and diseases of oil, and skin diseases;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their health is that the patient should remove his hair by twisting it with no rope, as I have described above;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then the patient and also the sick one, and a little of the long flame a little of the wide flame, for there is no fire.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	If the flames are too sharp, then break them up.
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	Then make a fire of blood, as much as you need to, and then tie it with wool, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The pain of the vein that runs through the neck is so great with water and sudden fever, and with diseases of the face, as headaches and red eyes that come into the face, even when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the quality of pain is that the patient strangles his throat, then takes hold of the long delicate flame, and puts it between the two nostrils because the vein does not open well on its own, and now it will start to run;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not burn too much in the process, and let the blood flow according to your need, then leave it alone for a night, because it is soon healed;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	is as follows:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The pain of the two armpits is helped by stretching the breast, and by the trouble of milking, and by many diseases, and by hemorrhoids, and by blisters, and it is said;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the qualities of health are such that the patient dislodges his neck from side to side, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and the master standing over the head of the patient, and the patient cutting one side of a vein, then he heals the vein long and slightly, then treating blood from time to time until it is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then he does the same on the other side, then he ties the vein, and draws it out slightly so that the patient does not strangle;
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and leaves it until morning so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of animals
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	For the health of the lips: they help to clean in the mouth, and prevent decay of the gums, and splits in the lips, and diseases of the teeth and tongue.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of health are such that the patient sits before you, and dislodges his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then he turns the lip and looks at the veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left, and you can recognize them because they are black, and because there are small veins that are black inside of them;
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	So both of them, and if you don't know them, and if you are in doubt, then do the largest one of each pair, and also do the two veins that are above and below, for it is a middle way.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	For the health of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	So the veins that are below the tongue, then after the treatment of the cerebral vein, which is for the extraction of the throat, and to the diseases of the eye, and to the diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the patient if that the disease is between your hands before the sun, and let the tongue lie, and look down on each side a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	So both of them, and do not go too much to perfection, for the veins are below.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins that you treat commonly are treated according to two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	ou em poinçon à tout i flamme mirton large, ou olivière subtil si com coutés trenchens, et est appelé «anésil»;
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and subtle according to the width and stretching of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame is called a 'mirtle', and it is wide as you see it.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the knotted veins that appear flat and contain thick blood and turmoil;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the flame olive:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more subtle pointed, and is for saving the veins that are subtle, where there is subtle blood yellow.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The blood from the base of the nose, which is one of these veins, goes to the throat, neck, chest, and abdomen;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it comes to the patient who bleeds profusely and who warms himself with the artery that is outside of it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	If he severs the artery, and the blood flow comes, if he needs to stop the bleeding, so as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and must not be grabbed by the flame, but cut off like this.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the base of the tooth does not open clearly, then you should extract it and change to another.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or if there is no pain in it, or if you feel pain in the vein when you press on the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	then the tooth opens clearly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and hold it to the flame as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you can feel the pulse clearly, then you should extract the arm, touching the spot until you feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the spot with a pin, and then extract the arm, pressing the vein with the flame as we have said;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and be careful not to hurt yourself in the artery when you mark the spot, because it is an artery.
eschui la donques.	I have received.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see coming out on top as the urine of a child, and his blood is red and thin, know that it is his artery.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry up then, and place your ear closely, then lift up your ear if it gets stiff, because it often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	Let him raise his arm, and leave it like that, and do not move the patient;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be afraid, and do not move him until he is well.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if his arm is not stiff and he comes to you, and the medicine is not given to him, if the artery is opened, for the head of the shoulder will be dislocated.
et estainche li sans.	and let it stiffen again.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of fig tree, and burn it, and take one of the halves and place it well until the other day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if he has no fever, that's good;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, if the doctor, as we said, of the powders that stop bleeding;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stopping of blood is not too great in several situations for the small wound of the leg, and the ability of the vein of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The bloodletting in the middle is good if it stops the bleeding from the head and the heart, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and the doctor should cut through the nerve that is at the back, and if he cuts too much in perfection, the nerve will burst, and the wound will be painful and perhaps cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any person by its fineness, you must cut it with the dull tool;
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and I abstained from the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two knees, then cut it short.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The relief of the cephalic pain, so that he does not go down to the head and supports the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to hit the olive flame or the merlin flame, for this is the one that saves all veins, because it does not damage the nerve or the artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek the lighter one first, and do not harm anything if you fail the first time, and you start again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and in case it injures some men, if you fail the first time, but it does not harm anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the relief depends on your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you must know about healing, if healing is only achieved to preserve health and prevent diseases from coming.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let the healing be done in one of the three veins that are or hurt:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	This is what the text says: 
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one must keep to the fast of priests for nine days and in autumn and winter after supper when the sign of satiation appears.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one must abstain from food on the first day or third day, for two hours or three times a day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The fast which is combined with illness has no fixed duration, but when need arises it must be maintained day and night in all hours.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and children should not fast until they are twelve years old, nor women carrying a child for four months until seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Doctors should not treat very old people who are over sixty years old.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when anyone does fast, in whatever way, it is necessary that he vomit the contents of a light clistere if he has repressed wind, so that the veins do not draw in the excess of putrid and harmful matter to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k'il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	do not heal those who are too exhausted by meat, or by wine, as much as it may be necessary, or by dropsies; and if someone is healed after a colic, vomiting, cramping of the belly, frequent visiting of women, labor, staying up late, and all other physical activities, or due to something done with the knife or the heart;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then carefully adjust the humors, because he will become fat, through meat, drink, and medicine, if you have it;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then let him take a bath or a dip, if anything does not benefit him, to gently remove the blood from the back of the neck between the third and fourth vertebrae, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep him away from work, drinking, lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and so are the bones and joints, and let the surgeon stand higher than the one on whom he operates, and rub his arms twice or three times, then remove the ligature gently, for when it is too tight or weak, he cannot do it without pain.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the wound with his hands until the veins swell and can be felt.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	and then moisten the surgeon's flame with a little old oil, and then put his left hand on that vein to stop the bleeding a little or where he wants to cut, so that the vein does not bleed while he cuts.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that run like strings for the surgeon, and some that are so thin with wind that when you put fire on them, if you take it away quickly, they do not bleed, and thus you are from those.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he opens the vein, if the wound is too narrow, for in these things it is necessary that the surgeon be wise.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if he opens the vein the first time, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, then begin again a little on the edge or above the wound, if the limbs are not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limbs are swollen and the patient hopes to get well, let him rest for a day or two, and do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	so that it may come to a head.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not enter or bathe, and then begin the operation if he likes it;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the fracture is small, or the bone slightly broken and you doubt that it will come out at all, then with great care and skill, break it again entirely;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and work a little healing, so that the legs are swollen.
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for this happens often, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the leg swollen, do not recommend medicine, and put on a little oil, because it soothes the body of the blood, and is soft in that place where the oil lies; because oil is soft in this place.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and administer the oil to each wound that you heal the veins, so as to stop up the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and it also makes a treble and bowing noise when put on the leg;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	so that it is subtle and moves apart when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there is a large abscess, which happens often, unless the wound has been well treated only once or the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and put on the leg a wet sponge with some heat and a little oil, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the flow of blood from a vein, and if it stays in place after a few days without any discoloration or browning, then it does not harm me;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on anything of aloe or myrrh made into a paste with juice of calamus, marjoram, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times an abscess and appearance occur to the blood from the temple:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	So then put your hand on it, and if you find the joint soft to the touch by pressing with your thumb, then this is the appearance of illness.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	So do not put on anything of what we have said, for perhaps in a short time there will be no artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but the king makes it dry by curing it with another cure until it is well.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat every wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if it is black inside, then let it go out until it is red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see a lump, let it be thin.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for those who are sick and have to extract blood, we make the wound larger and wider flames.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for those who are weak, do the opposite, heal them little by little, and heal them by cutting across, not by piercing;
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this way of healing saves from the decay of blood and the entanglement of nerves, and it is better than long healing or wide healing.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for those whose hearts are in need of healing, one should give moist wine made from pomegranate juice.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	if it is heated, give III or IV times the juice; and if it is of cold complexions, moisten it before healing with honey syrup or aromatic syrup made with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and sweet syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he sweats in health, after the flow of blood, then it is fitting that he smell brew of wine and subtle aromatic syrup, and use the other things which we have said in the chapter or composition for fainting, to evacuate the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he vomits up his food and is healthy again, then it is fitting that he is healed little by little according to the quantity of his continuing virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who vomits after the first wound, and has a strong fever, if he heals seven hours after the first wound, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who vomits in another place, should he heal on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For there is blood coming from within the body that causes fever.
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	If a large amount of blood is drawn and the hole enlarged so that it leaks a lot through the skin;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then you shall treat all the symptoms of disease, and place your hand on his pulse when he is healthy, so that death does not come from the skin, and this happens many times, when the healing is neglected;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and do not wait until you see that the arm has dislocated again, and make the blood come out a second time, and the hole is closed, so that you press firmly on it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	do not do this if it is bent, for that would be wrong;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but leave it until he has healed a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you may apply fire to the tip until the blood that has been frozen at the vein's opening comes out again, and place thereon a small piece of rope soaked in water, and press gently.;
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has burst, let it go and do not constrict it, as long as the abscess is drained.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if need be, to drain the blood a second time, if the vein is in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein that runs through the arm is attached to the vein at the base of the head because it is complex.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the way of healing is such that the patient dips his hand in hot water until the veins turn red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then he should move it gently so that the vein is visible clearly, then now treat it with a needle, not from the wide end nor the long end;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and if the break is wide, and if you heal it well near the joint of the hand, and so he cannot get out of it, then put the hand in hot water, and let the blood run in the water until enough has passed;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is swollen, then don't dip the hand in hot water again, because you put it in more danger than when it was swollen;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the healing of this vein is safer than all other veins, neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The healing of the savings of the right hand is worth all the diseases of the liver, and this is the way:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	extirp the hand, and pour hot water on it, as long as the vein is gone, if we can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if he has a sore throat, and cuts off all of it, so that it does not hurt anything;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not trim it too much, for the nerves are all exposed and then put the hand in hot water again, if it has frozen in the wound, and cannot pull it out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary, put oil and thread on it to hold it tightly together, and do the same for each finger.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The medicine for the left hand is good for the disease of the mouse; and do the same as I told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The medicine of the Sophene is good for all diseases that come about in the body, as are diseases of the feet, retention of wind, disease of the kidneys, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of his throat is that the patient pours some water on it again and rubs on the vein until it stops bleeding, and lays on top of the joint at the foot.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and if the vein is at the ankle, and above it go many ways;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	he should cut where it is wider or narrower, or at the ankle, so that he does not hurt himself.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you cut on the leg, if you keep away from the nerves that are exposed, and also cut in such a way as when you are chopping.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the flames be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot get them out, put the foot back into the water, and let the vein bleed well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if you cut it for the first time, if you start again a little higher up on top because the blood is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt about the nerves, as we have said, and so do with the other leg evenly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The leg of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle and its pain goes up to the knee when it is for pain.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of the cut is that the patient goes in or bath, and extracts from the ankle IV fingers by twisting, because otherwise it does not open the vein;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, then cut it in all ways that you can, and crossing;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and wait until you have chopped it, for the blood is flowing, and it is very much repinned by many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you don't treat it, so that there is no rain from him who opens or closes the foot, and towards the small toe, and keep away from the nails;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and make so much heat of the wound that you see, and then untie the bandage, and put on cotton and hold it in place;
ele est maintenant sanee.	And he is now cured.
des sainies de ventouse	the suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Vapourizers are made of horn, or of air, or of glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and the ventilation is done according to two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by hurting and drawing blood, or without hurting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this ventilation that is without hurting is according to two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either it is all fire, or not fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and the ventilation that is made by hurting and drawing blood is done in 12 places of the body, so that one is all on top;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the other is broken at the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and the other two are in the two coasts of the collar;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the ventuse dislociates the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the ventuse dislocates the two shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the ventuse on the back;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the ventuses dislocate the two arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the ventuses dislocate the two legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the ventuses dislocate the two ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the ventosis does not treat blood when it is a small opening that is scattered in the vessel, and for this reason it does not harm anyone, if only because of the small openings that are scattered in the sea;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	nor does it suffice if she is administered, nor does it matter if there is any disease that comes from overconsumption, as long as the whole body is empty;
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of diseases one needs to be ventosed, or for habits, we administer it every hour in the beginning of the month, and at the end, and also on a daily basis;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are those who, when they have to go outside, become very heavy.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And if it is so that those who are vendoring have repletion and reddening in their face, and in their chief, and at their neck, and darkness of eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	And those who are vendoring have a drop of blood in their mouth, and have escaped the tongue, and thirst for blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if it is so that those who are dreaming, and see with bloodless eyes and confused vision and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even more so when it is hot in the month of July, we order them to be vented after three hours from daybreak.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The physician of the moon helps with the headache at the head ... that comes to the eyes, and it should not come except after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this vendoring is in the place of the physician of the head, and it should not come except from those who are of a cold disposition and who have taken a chill, for this does them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and so it is not appropriate for me to sleep without using it, nor those who have or chief cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are cured often become dizzy, and so it is necessary to place the cup a little lower by doubt of dizziness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The ventilation of the neck is in place of the main vein and the base of the skull, and for this reason it is used for the extraction of the tooth, and for cutting through the jaw, and for all, and for filling;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and so it should be pressed hard because if it holds too tightly, then a stomach or gut or body part will break.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The two ribs of the neck are painful to touch, and they cause blindness and headaches, and choke, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and are in place of the main vein of the base of the skull;
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and you should command the physician that he press his hand on the place, so that he does not hit the artery, and does not disturb the blood flow.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The winds that blow from the front are very harmful to the mouth, and to the decay of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and is in the position of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windsations of the shoulders are worth illness that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The winds that blow from the front are as harmful as three veins in the arms, because they draw away blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And instruct the patient that he not cut too deeply, because his vein is exposed and vulnerable; it can easily be cut and bleed profusely.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The wind that blows from the back is very harmful to the fundament and to the decay; it is necessary that the wind be great and wet, because it has the duty of milking well.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	And if it should become subtle, then it would break;
et i fai grans plaies.	and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The legs' windfalls open so widely because they draw blood from all the body, and are the cause of old pains in the kidneys, in the uterus, and in the bladder, and shake the flowers;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and are in the second position of the feet, and the second of the ankles, but nevertheless they weaken the body after a long use, and produce more than two diseases.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The manner of applying the suction cup is that you put it first in a clear place, and suck quickly, and then place it firmly, move evenly, and do not cease doing this until you see the red and inflamed place, and appear the color of blood;
