puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then dry it off, and put on the suction cups again, and take care in the arrangement of the bodies, for there are some who have very hard skin, and they get sore quickly:
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	if it is necessary to hurt once only, and make large wounds, and a little deep;
et suce legierement.	and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the sinew is thick, if it is necessary to hurt twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time for diluting the blood of the big vein.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	and if it is very thick, then it is necessary to hurt the third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to extract blood little by little, if we only press once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	and if we want to take a lot of blood, then we start again and again;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the blood is thick, then we press hard and completely, and the end is that the gush of blood is sudden, and it covers someone who has thick and tough skin, and who has been burned, you should grease the leprous areas with oil that opens and dissolves:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in an open wound, of violet oil, or of sweet almond oil, or of cucumber seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in the eye, of watercress oil, or of lily, or of chamomile, or other thing that seems suitable.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if it is too cold and oily, take oil of almonds, or of balsam, or oil of anise, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if they have a sore that is dry and large, then it is not necessary to put oil on, but it is necessary to wash it after the cooling of rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberries, or water of cucumbers, or water of porcelain, or other things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has moisture, if it dries up like this, or with water of myrtle, and of sumach, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have great excesses rise up from old wine, or from water of suet, or from aneth or chamomile decoction, or other like things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and it is not convenient to take a bath before the vacuum, but after the bath an hour or two;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and do not sleep after the vacuum is taken, and it is convenient that he warm up when he should be vacuumed and when he has been vacuumed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And guard against those who are healing from colic, and if the sun is too high and heated;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it is convenient that he eat cold things, as pomegranates, endive, and lettuce at the edge, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and soft porridge, and cheese of goat's milk, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion, if they eat syrup of honey, and fragrant wine that is between old and new, and soft porridge, and soft porridge and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and as he grows older, if he must drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give to some men once or twice pepper or musk before the ventilation, or after, to strengthen the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and be subtle in his drink, but it is necessary that only those who are warm drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The ventosas that are put to hurt are those that are put on the liver, and the kidney, and the podagre, and the belly, and the buttocks, and the rain and the hainche, for this member does not suffer to be hurt on the outside, and we put it on the breasts when it is not healthy;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to remove the viscous fluid that is in the member, as we put ventosas on the belly and the buttocks to ease the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain, when there is an operation or stone, if it removes by its attractive virtue the operation, or moves away the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and so when one puts it on the liver and the mouse as it is retained wind, and these suction cups are emptied clean for suckling only;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and never are they put together fire, nor any times plainness of water, if as the disease of pleurisy, and in such a way one fills the suction cup with hot water or water in which he has boiled herbs suitable for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup administered to fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it has II width of a half palm of parfont, and has where it goes around the middle I small hole, as for to put in a needle, and is of air, before so that it does not wound the patient when one puts it on the member;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and in the middle is a staff of air or iron, to take a grip, and there are great and small ones according to the diseases and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the suckers of children are other than those of old people, and skinny than fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must put this suction on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	Take the wax candle or ointment, and put it between the suction cup and the limb: let the clarity be at the bottom of the suction cup so that it doesn't burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the limb, and your hands must be in the pit that we have said: so that when one sucks, if there is steam, and take off the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take the ointment as before, and renew it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup that has been used for pleurisy disease, there is no need for a wick or pit, and it is only used when it is plain of water, and put on the limb only slightly;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	are not created with such small members that they cannot be put into a cup for their smallness, as the lips and gums and similar things;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in their nakedness of limbs, as the deer and does and others;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of using them so is that when you find limps that are in clear fresh waters without danger, then take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them into a pot in fresh water, as long as they are friendly and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be healed with the cup and the vacuum, then rub the member until it is red, and put the limps on;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are clear, and have 치유, then it is put on, for this is worth more later.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the limb up, and then of water, very well, and then squeeze it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if he leaves his back too long after the chest of the swines, so that it is moistened by a cold drape, and put on, as long as the swine is swollen.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if he has many swines, so put on vitriol powder, or scabs, and similar things, as long as they are swollen.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or put on half a handful of peeled peas, and leave them to burn at the fire, so now they will cool down.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you have more work, then take other swines.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the swines will not take it, so frolic the fire of the blood, or put there a needle as long as the swine gives off blood, and then put them on, and soon as they feel the blood, so burn.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are squealing, so sprinkle on a little powder of aloes and sawdust, or ashes, so they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	The chapter of calumny is necessary many times in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of a fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know then, you sons of bitches, that the wise men are soaked in this chapter, that you will never find such a thing in any of the old books or letters.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, the science is strange to us in our land, for I have never found any good one.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and know nothing, except that by the science of ancient books, where I have studied so much and treated the science, and by experience, and by the custom of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described in this chapter what is contained therein, and has summarized it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I did in the two chapters above.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is fitting that we say in this book the sums of speech and the chapters where wisdom sets forth her understanding, and holds fast to truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture, dislocation, twist, or strain comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hurry to save the patient from both sides, unless something stops him entirely, as in the case of a weak neck, or an obstruction, or an old man;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	If he is very thin, or too often hungry,
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and do not drink any cold wine, nor any fatty foods, and do not fill yourself too much with meat that fills the veins with blood, as long as you have no doubt about the heat of the abscess, or the expansion of the substance in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the patient returns to their normal way of life without considering these things.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that the patient be nourished with meats that produce great thickness, or viscosity, like cooked flour in water, and rice, and eggs, and pies made from goat's milk, and cheese, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with great nutrition healing begins more quickly and sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones broken from old age or frail people cannot recover or harden the limbs according to their nature because of the lack of blood in the members, nor those that are too soft, as with the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but do not heal, return to the broken bone and large joints that join the limb together, as much as it hardens as it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and not at all of his work, and for this it is necessary to feed him with large meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the breakers are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is other than the break of the foot or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes to the shoulder, and another in twisting, as if the cutting of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break that is all a small fracture.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each has its own device, and its own specific tool for restoration, according to what the memory comes back in place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and is understood the breaking of the bone because its edge is twisted, and open well from the side, and presses by the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no torus, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can have torus, or split, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you cannot move it by hand alone, but put on medicine that comes here after, and then restrained now gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the break which has happened in the arm, and are the two parts separated, it is now necessary to put them in an equal way, so that the nails come out;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and when the nails come out, if he leaves no gap, as long as the abscess is calmed down;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	and then make it equal to the wound that you can easily and cleanly, and know that the restoration of it is lighter than the restoration of him who has pieces;
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	and then hold it, as it is convenient hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are pieces broken, if the extension of the two parts is short or long, whether it is hand or foot, or a small member, or two strings, or one string and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the member according to its natural form, so that when the parts of the broken member are restored, you restore them by all means to their places as easily as you can, and keep that by your work no injury or pain comes to the patient;
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and join well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it well in the hand if it seems to you that it is not right:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If the dressing is applied well and not too much, and do not press it as those who bring it about by their ovraige, an abscess hot and contracted to the limb, as we have often wanted.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limbs are in place, so that the patient does not move it, neither waking nor sleeping, turning or in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and keep the limb well secured so that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when one feels no pain, then it is not in place, and it is necessary to put it in such a position that one feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and guard so that it is placed correctly, so that there is no tortuosity when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the limb is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken member is diverse in smallness and greatness and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, as arms and legs and similar things:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	If it is necessary to wrap linens that are soft and fine.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those who are thick, such as the thigh and leg:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	If it is necessary to wrap with a broad and sturdy linen, because the broad linen envelops the entire limb, holding it evenly from all sides so that there is no itchiness;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then tie it lightly, three or four times according to the limb, and hold one hand on all of the linen, then go up above the break and hold it less, so that the break comes a little away;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the linen little by little, until you press a great deal of the skin, then take another linen and wrap it very tightly above the break;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the sore part of the break and hold it with moderate pressure, not too strong or too gently, as we said in the first line above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	and place between the linen threads or drapes, as long as they are all even, then tie it tightly above the bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	If there is swelling or an abscess, place something soothing on the abscess to soothe it and let the swelling go down, and leave it like that for a few days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then put your splints on, and let them be of half a cane of sawn wood, or of a beam, or of palm leaves, and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the splint that one puts on the break is a little thicker and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be also as far away as necessary for the limb's size, whether small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	and stretch on the poles also as you did in the first hour, then tie up above it a thread forwardly, as in the first hour on the fracture.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	then narrow it up, gradually lessening the tightness.
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and let the thread be light, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, as I have seen in the works of foolish men who make ropes out of linen twine, and that is a great mistake, because the length cannot be equal if it is too thin, and it only deserves to be less than half an inch between each pole.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the hooks of the stars after extraction in their healthy state, then let them be bound with linen, or another kind of rag, so that they do not get cut.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bruise, and the cure is broken, I will describe the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to extract stars from all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it is not fitting to put poles before five or seven days, or more according to the urgency of the abscess, which sometimes heats up suddenly.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and consider the method of the ancient empirics in restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and it is that you take flour that holds on the walls of the mill, and confound it with much honey, and put this confection, not too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the plaster restoring the fracture to many dispositions, especially to women and small children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another way of the plaster restoring the fracture and the dislocation and the twist:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	take 3 ounces of alum and 2 ounces of saltpetre and nettle and asafetida and gum arabic and myrrh, mixed;
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	myrrh and aloe, mixed;
alechil VIIII З.;	alchich
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make it into a powder, and mix it with honey of bees;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the patient's complexion is warm, then use this plaster, for it is of good composition and restores broken bones quickly, and is useful to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Other way to cauterize than by fire:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take mugwort and vinalda, half a pint.
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	Mirrortree and aloe, half a pound.
acaice VI З.;	Ointment, six drams.
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Boil the arnica well and grind it with oil or plenty of vinegar, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Other way to cauterize joints and broken bones from their place, and to soothe the pain immediately, and to trim the bone, and the wound:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take another new, and moisten it with boiled oil, and put on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Cysts do not respond well, but they are good for soothing abscesses and properly relieving pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Other way to cauterize which restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves and earth-paeony leaves, grind them together, and make an ointment.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to make an ointment for healing bone breaks and reducing the swelling of an abscess: take fresh milk and mix it with wine, then apply it to the affected area.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of vinalda, chamomile, violets' flowers, flour of vitre, each a part;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and crushes, and mixes with wine, and heats the members, mixing them with water of coriander or vinegar, and uses it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to make an ointment that is more effective than the first one, which is used when the abscess is persistent and difficult to heal: take milk, wine, and water, each in equal parts, and apply it hot to the affected area.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of marsh-mallow, and linseed, mullein, mallowe, and fennel grass, and flowers of violet and chamomile, each one part;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and crushes, and mixes with salt water or sweet water or wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, I hypocras says that one should not put anything on the broken member before it is healed, except a cerote made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he said that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to me that one should put on the broken member, to restore it, dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way to burnish that is good for wounds and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take muck and straw of cows, or feathers of geese, and marsh-mallow, and string it evenly, crushing it, and making it into a paste and lying on it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then he undoes it after one day, and takes care that the patient feels no pain, and that his bone does not move from its place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	If they do not dislodge by their own hand.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if the pain comes to a head, or itchiness, or a restlessness or swelling occurs, if you hurry and dislocate it, and apply the poultice now;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a light cloth, and a sponge of sea water moistened, and dip it in the water, and raise it to the head, as long as the itchiness ceases, and the pain is soothed;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the member rest for an hour, then put on another dry cloth, wet with water or oil of roses, and tie it to a pole, as long as you are sure of the abscess heating up;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and let the inflammation of the member rest, and be eased of pain, then begin to dislocate again gently, and a little bit of ointment, and do not dislocate it as strongly as before;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and carefully as long as he is well.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is chafed and red and painful and swollen all around it, and you have to use poultices and ligatures, then start again, just as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	If the limb does not respond to any of the above treatments, then do not dislocate it until after three, four, five, or seven days.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and never let it rest for more than twenty days, according to what one observes, until the break-up of the joint appears, and approach the dislocation of the shoulder with care;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then take even greater care than before, and let his meat grow thicker, as I have said above;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and know that if the skin dries up more than is necessary, it cannot be moved;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then rise immediately after each dislocation, and do so every third day, and let the shoulder rest for a moment;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	For in this work, cut off the skin carefully around the limb, and gently remove what is loose, so that the limb may return to its normal position;
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	It is unwholesome, and if it is done out of fear, and I see no other thing than to make it loose and do it right.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various ways to break up
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of breaking, and various shapes, and the causes are different.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	For it has fractures that are made by the impact of a sword, and the neck bone is broken all the way down to where it joins the body, so much so that it comes off like a stump;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and this is called "hematoma".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	or the sword pierces the bone from above, and it is called  "absolute" fracture.
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and it is the wound of those two great fractures or one small fracture.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	Or if there is percussion inside, or an edge, or a collarbone of stone, or falling on stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a breaking that approaches the tendon which is over the bone, or is under it, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that closes in the bone as fine as hair, and it is called a "capillary" fracture.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound is made by a stone or by falling, or by some other thing, and brings in a piece of bone; and if the joint is dislocated as the blacksmith does to the kettles when he shapes them.
si entre li piere dedens.	if between the stone inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And if there is more moisture at the top who have or head moist bones, like the head of a child;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it has all these ways of fracture that small pieces are lost as if they were stars;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will talk to him in his place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all kinds of fractures by traction on them, and by the inspection of wounds, and by the cart that is before it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair appearance is caused by this: when one has uncovered the bone, and rubbed it in, thus opening the black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure for the fracture, take care as to the accidents of the disease, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting, loss of understanding, extension, paleness, feverishness, or hair growing furiously red and other similar signs in many conditions, so it cannot be healed by doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any hopeful accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the birth comes first to you, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at most that you can do.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue around the bone may not decay, and the accident that we have spoken of may come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone comes just to the membrane that covers the skull, so that you bend the bent part thus:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and is that you squeeze the head of the sick person, and uncover it on the bone in all ways that you can, and on the figure of the wound more easily than you can, and let the blood come out at the cover of the bone or at the abscess, help yourself to what is necessary, and is that you fill the place with wet towels in oil of rose;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and let the wound rest as long as the abscess is calm, and be sure of the evacuation of blood;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin to pierce the bone, and it is done according to two ways of work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one way is that you cut at a narrow angle at the front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I bottle another way more than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second way is that you have many different lengths of blades, some narrow and others wide, and sharp, and made of iron:
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and in work lightly, so that you do not blister the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and tough, it is necessary that you pierce it from inside, so that you introduce blades with tangents, not completely through so as not to pierce the bone's end, and must have above the point a margin or circle, so that the point does not pass beyond the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you will have many, so that each one comes back to its place in the end of the bone, so that you are patient for all tests.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And this is the form of the three ways to be patient:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality for piercing between the bones is that you put the stop in place on the bone, and turn it back to its two positions as you know that the bone has been pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then put the stop on the other side again a little way apart and so do all around, then cut out the space of the bone that is between the pits, and do it more finely than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you bring the bone to your hand, or to any of the tools that you have there, such as tweezers, pincers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and make sure that you do not touch the skull or the medicine;
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone and treated it, if you can see that you need to remove the marrow which is delayed in the bone from all other instruments resembling an incisors, but it must be more pliable and finer than the other incisor.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if there is no delay in any small bones, nor scales, if the bone is lightly held to the instruments;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then heal the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other way to treat it is that which Galen says, which is more effective;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and the fire very hot, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you discover a part of the bone, where the break is open; so that when you have discovered that part, you put the head of this lens-shaped incision there, from which it gets its shape.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side, and this side is water in two places, so that the cutting is towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	and then hammer a small mallet on top, so that you lightly chop the bone all around, and be very careful of the splinters which are scattered;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it's broken to the bone, then the bone is a little injured, because a strong bone causes pain and discomfort.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is wet in two sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then hit with a small mallet on top, so that you lightly tap the bone all around, and take good care of the tendon that is attached to it; if it is caught on the bone, then carefully cut the bone, for one cuts the bone well without hurting, and without fear.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you are dealing with very sharp razors, and then with even sharper ones, and do not stop doing this as long as it is necessary.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other hair-splitting and subtle wounds, you must proceed according to their alignment.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	This is not something that can be easily fixed by someone who has not studied this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is suppurating, you must take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, dip it in oil and put it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another cloth, double it II or III times, dip it in wine and oil and put it on top of the first cloth;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do it as lightly as you can so that you don't aggravate the wound, then cover it with another cloth, and don't peel it off until it has healed completely;
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and let it remain so for a day or two, until the abscesses are calm, then remove it, and administer medicines as roots of licorice, flour of times, incense powder, aristaology, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and of these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and administer medicines immediately without stinging;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and guard that the wound be clean, so you don't let it get infected, nor do you let it gather bowels, for when the bowels gather on the cloth of the skull, if they are cut and torn, they cause great harm to the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when one puts a mordant medicine on it, it burns from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if black comes out only because of the medicine that has been put on it, and its virtue is such, then you should squeeze a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and one drape of rosin, and put it on the medicine;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then the cure by the methods he knows how to do until he is well.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that the two parts of the neck above are never broken, or one by itself, because they are bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and this cartilage does not break unless it is forced or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must insert your little finger or nipple of the neck, and make it even with your index finger at the back, until the neck regains its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do it lightly, so that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the neck, and cannot come back to its place, then you must put it right with a small stick at the top of the neck.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if he is broken in two places, then do otherwise, and hurry to restore the first part the next day if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or ninth day, when the abscess has calmed down, then insert at the top of the neck a few strips of linen cloth, if the break is in one place.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	And you put one on top of the other on another side, if it breaks.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let the tents be so large that they fill the apertures from which they come.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And no one should restore it without wetting the strips first; each day they must be changed.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem good to me, but it is necessary that they be wet in the preparation of ash of ovend and powder of mill;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the tent, until the bone is hard and the cartilage is hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And never put goose feathers in the place of tents, and if it is a sodden drape, and holds the break, and blows the sickness about.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Or fare a lieu de quille une branche d'arbre, et la tige pendante; et la tige ne tienne pas par le haut, mais seulement par le bas avec des visages de bois;
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if the abscess comes to birth while you are working, put cotton soaked in oil or a string of hempen twine or a piece of silk; or
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if an abscess forms, so that it is pus, then put there by the side, flour of sizings, and powder of incense, prepared with ash of ovend, then put on light poultices, and do not bind the lou nes;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if his break is small, he is broken into small pieces, so extract with the suitable instruments to him, then cut the fracture, and the cure of things injangling car, and souding, yes as plasters and ointments suitable to him;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if he has no pain inside his neck at all, if he cures the tens, and puts wires of lead, as long as he is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the breaking of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken and there is no wound, and the break is not very deep, and it is not shattered into two pieces, but rather twisted inside, then one should handle it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is convenient, if his break is on the right side, that you put your index finger in the mouth of the patient.
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if his break is on the left jaw, if you put your index finger of your right hand into it, and push the break in gently, and make it equal with the other hand from the side, and make it long.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jaw is on the second side, then it is fitting that you equalize the two sides with an extension, until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the movement inside is, or a tear, if you extract it with a gold, silver, or silk thread, then put the wax on the broken jaw, and put a double cloth.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and on the loins put a great well-made shield, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it to the neck where you can, and order the patient that he rest, and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the figure changes, so let it rest for three days, and then put back in place what has changed;
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and apply plaster to it, with powder from the mill with much chalk or flour of buckwheat, after you have removed the cast;
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and on the plaster another light lining, and if the plaster hurts, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it as long as it is healthy;
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	is sometimes healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses arise, if you administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and a wound together, do not remove any piece of the bone when the wound is healed;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	If subtle of the ostrich are suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is tight, if you open it by fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et when you have boned all these pieces, and there is no delay, so to cool the wound, if it is wide, and put on it I bandages suitable for this, in order to ease the pain, as long as it is healed.

Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The breaking of them several times before, against the shoulder, and the break is according to three manners:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	where it is broken and dislocated in two, and there are pieces, and it is the easiest to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	where there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work if it is so that the break is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds up the shoulder that was broken by the force of the break;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the neck towards the part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then set the break even on both sides so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or hair-splitting;
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you have more to stretch, so stretch the shoulder of the patient with a round stake of cloth or linen, and make it big according to your need;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and hold it firmly, and hold the needle in your hand, so that you make an even hole, as is right.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot remove the head of the pole at the end, so that it comes out perfectly, it is necessary that the patient lie down on his back, and place the shoulder pole horizontally, and put the ministers' shoulders under it, until the bone of the pole is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then place the break on your two hands, and if you find debris, then it is necessary that you split above;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and try to press the pieces together lightly, and if the bone cannot join for any reason, then put the cap on one of the incisions that you have made;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but that you remove the needle this instrument, to protect the patient.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and seems like a spoon, and is not hair-like, and should also be as wide as it is necessary for the size of the bone and the ability of the work;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and has two heads, as you see, and one is wide and the other narrow, like the break in the wound that you made when you broke the bone;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are confident of the temperature of the abscess, if the wound is small, or you doubt about the temperature of the abscess, if the wound is covered with linen and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses come, if it has oil in it, and water and vinegar, and put on it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The extraction of the bone, when there are wounds and lacerations, is that you put on the bone the plaster from the powder of the mill and the owl's dung, and lightly apply it, and put a spike on the joint if you need to do so.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	then take a very long band of a palm's width, then put two layers of linen cloth over it, and the plaster.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	then take a thin stick of three fingers' width and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that the top of the bandage is even.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and put the stick on the break in the bone, and turn the bandage over the neck, and extract the joint cleanly, and extract the ill joint.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and the dislocation of each part, and when you see that the opening holds the broken bone in place, and you clearly see that the spine does not move over the broken bone, if it is reduced every day, and when the ligature is removed, if it is restrained;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and place the patient on their back, and put a small board under the shoulder, in order to raise the dislocated part upwards;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	if the fracture of the arm is eased by the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and no bad accident comes about, until 20 days have passed;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then start the treatment again if you see that it is necessary, and hold him back and leave him like that until he has recovered;
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and she has been restored in 28 days, and in some men less.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	But if the shoulder is broken, or out of place and does not move smoothly, and it only hurts when touched.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	If you reset it according to its natural shape, and do so in all possible ways that you can.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	Then put on the shoulder with a powder of the mill, with plenty of flour, and light strokes, and put it in a double drape.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then put on a large and thin board, a little wider than the shoulder, and descale it at the edge of the shoulder, if you employ the hair of the cloth, so that the board is even.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then tie it with a large and strong bandage, so that the board does not move from its place, and inspect it every day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And each time that it moves, if you tie it again, and make the board even if it is out of place, and let the patient lie on his back.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	And the shoulder is reset in XX days or in XXV.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the number of days is completed, if it dislocates again, and be careful, for it is not bone that moves so easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone projects forward, and there is no smooth surface to stop it, then make it up and bone it over, and do as we said in the breaking of the jaw to relieve an abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the pie
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The feet are never broken in midair, but this happens sometimes;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	But it often breaks at the bottom.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, if it leans towards the side, and causes great pain to the patient, and there is no alane [a kind of plaster], then sometimes it vomits blood, and opens the veins in the broken bone, and it smells bad.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the reset so that the patient lies on his back, and put a cushion between his shoulders, then press the shoulders together, and carefully join the ribs with your hands, and adjust them in every way as well as you can, until the bone figure is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Then put on plasters and stoppers above it with subtle salt or another light stuff, and wrap it in a garment, and lay it on the broken bone, so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the loins smoothly to the back, and hold it forward, and release each hour, and if it relaxes, so hold it.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it is necessary to separate it, because of corrosion or because of itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, if you hurry, and separate it, and scrape the plaster, and apply it in a way suitable for treatment;
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then remove the plaster, and hold it until it is healthy.
de la brisure des costes	the break of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the breaking of the ribs does not come except in large lumps behind the back, and at the top inward, and do not bend them too much except for those which are painful.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and the smell is good to the question how it was done.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And restore them so that you make the break even, as it is fitting.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put on plaster, and hold it with a stake, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the breaking of the ribs goes inward, then the patient feels great pain and a stinging sensation, as if it were crying, because the bone does not stretch the skin.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and let it cool with water, and every day and vomit great quantities of blood, and this is a deadly disease, and the old ones have great pain in their limbs.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if it is necessary to administer meat that swells the belly, in order to push the break away.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, unless hot absesses come, if it has not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, let the healthy one.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And they said that one should put leeches on the wound to draw out the pus, and this is apparently reasonable;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	However, doubt remains that leeches do not attract excess fluid to the wound due to their weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that we must cover the place with another moisture in oil, and put tents between the ribs to make the space even, then it is cured of the cure of plague, of meat, and of medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain in the bone that touches the wound, and doubt remains with the patient, then it is necessary to split the skin of the chest, and it is necessary to put a tool there to protect the wound;
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then one must cut the bone lightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound together, if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it is well.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if abscesses appear, if they are put on drapes soaked in oil and placed on the bed.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat while the head of this, which is due to an abscess, and is gizzing along the back or side where it is necessary, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break in the throat
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	No time comes that breaks the bones of the neck, and what happens is that he bleeds;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also at the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this has happened to anyone, and you can see whether he will be well or not, if you notice that his hands are softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, if he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is fatal in many cases, and if it does not move and feels well when it is stretched out, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient is cured, if one puts medicine on it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if similar things happen to the back, and you can not know whether it is healed or not, if the bones are softened, and if the accident that happened was due to a fall, and on the back has windiness and excretion without will;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when it is treated with a poultice on the belly, if there is windiness and excretion without will;
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is soothed on his back and he tries to move, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is deadly:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	If I don't work hard at my healing.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, it is the lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the cure is that if you treat an abscess with hot oil or oil of meadow mustard, until it is calmed down;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then put on one of the plasters, drying it and binding it with a bandage, and command the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and don't sleep in that part where he feels pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if some bone comes loose, if you cover it with poultice;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and set the bone, then join the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a stitch, then treat it with ointment made from vinegar, until it is healed;
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the bone of the shoulder is broken, which is called the "shoulder joint", pour out your poultice from your left hand, and hold it even with your right hand, then put on the plaster and wrap it up, if you need to;
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And hold it in place, and if there is an excess of bone, cut it off, and the bone, and heal the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	For the fracture of the shin bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	May it happen that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it happens, may there be only a little reduction at the head.
