et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	And make it long, and decline it in the parched, and comes to the patient pain at the place, and swelling, and that which breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the setting-right that is, you extend your hand upon it, as long as you are on the break;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and know what is the break and the form of it;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And if the break is at the head, let it be made equal, as long as it is in its natural form.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it declines inwardly, then make the patient lie on his stomach, as long as the setting in place of that break is convenient to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have made it equal, put on it a plaster, and then put on a wooden or wooden stake, and hold the break so that it does not move;
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and set the bones back together along the sides, as long as the hole is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on his side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if there is a fever, if it does not cause a fever, as long as the abscess is calm, and put on what we have said above;
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to restoration, and hold it firmly as necessary, if there is no bad accident;
et c’est li maniere.	This is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	For the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder accessory is that which is between the collar and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then one should restore it according to one of the two ways:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	where one is that you take a strong rope, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie two knots in the rope, and raise them up high, and cut the sick person on one side;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then tie some arms of the rope to the beam, so that it comes down to the ground, and take one end of the rope and hold it with a strong hand behind; then, after having raised him up with your feet, let him fall on his back;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then make the mirror even with his hands together, as it returns to him as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one sways the sick person on his back, and he lays his hand on his throat, then orders two ministers that one bleeds who is on the breeze-block with his hands, and the others bleeds all over the body, and extends each to its side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too strong, then strip off the flesh of the wound, and on the wound, and each minister extends to its side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the mirror is close to the shoulder blade, you should put a rope around the shoulder and another one across the chest, away from the mirror.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	And if the mirror is away from the chest, you should put the rope lightly, without effort, as the mirror is even on its side and on its height;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then make the mirror equal, as it should be, and hold it in place, so that the incisions do not move.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if the incisions have come, do not hold them in place for more than seven days, and put a wet cloth and oil on it, until the incisions are healed;
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Then hold it in place, and the way to hold it is that you put plaster on the mirror, then join the arm to the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or the chest;
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and wrap the cloth around it, and support on the shoulder, and on the arms so that the arm is in line with the elbow, if there is nothing to defend it or if the bone has not been broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use stakes, and place over the fracture a wider and stronger stake than the others, and keep between each stake two spaces, and make each stake as large as it passes three spaces on both sides.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then support on the stakes, so as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the paste over the fracture, stronger and less by moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the setting of the stakes and the support, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and doubt the incision, leave it tied for seven days, as we have said.
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	then watch each for three days that the itch does not spread to place, or that the healing does not come to the member because it is too constricted.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the adhesive, as we said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if such an accident does not happen, so that the dislocation is not relieved within three days or more, and the patient sleeps on his back, and has his hands on his stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and put a clean piece of linen around the shoulder with care that the figure of the member does not move, or that the ligaments are not relaxed;
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	if it is given by the virtue of medicine, and he is given the food that we have prepared in advance, in such a way that the food is at the first subtle level;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when it begins to recover, if it is heavy.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is proper that the shoulder and the leg should be recovered in ten days altogether;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And then he must untie and administer baths and medicines for relief.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the contraction is bad and tight, it should not be unbound for one or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "humerus," one of which is small, and this is the one that connects to the hand.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and this is the one that goes back towards the little bone.
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	Perhaps the large humerus can break alone, or perhaps the small one, and maybe both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small humerus is broken, the healing is easy, and so is the recovery;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	And when the large one is broken, the healing is bad, and more painful than when both are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small flail that is bruised only slightly, if it is necessary to stretch it lightly and make it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	If it's just the large humerus, then we need to extract it with force;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and stretch it out on a table, and turn the hand so that the thumb is higher than the other fingers, and the little finger lower than the others, and let the patient be stretched out across it, and the thigh in front of him higher up, so that the patient doesn't feel any pain;
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then extend the ministers their arms to the dislocation of the shoulder to his hand, or to his neck, and other ministers to another above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then make it even according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the breakage there are pieces, let each one be placed in its place, and if one of them does not hold fast to its place, you shall put a pin through it, and you shall not restore it to its place, but mend it on the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the breaking there is a wound, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter;
si pren la cure.	then take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if in the difficulty of restoration of the wound there are abscesses, then dip a cloth made of oil rosin and white wax, which is neither too hard nor too soft;
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and I will drape it gently over the top, until the abscesses are calm.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then the oil, and I put the plaster of the powder of the mill with a lot of wax, because put the splints, and the splint of the break is next to it, and a little more wide than the others;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that he should have six splints or arms in various positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	so that the fracture is in one of the bones, or in II.
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and stretch it over the break more than any other part, and always less by stretching, as I said at the beginning about the paste;
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the drape that are over the break be soft and wet, and not hard or rough;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let the fabric, which is stretched, be of linen, not too thick nor too fine, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And restore the member and the ligament after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if some bad accident comes to the limb, such as itchiness that comes to the limb, let it be soaked with lukewarm water until the itchiness is relieved;
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the limb rest neither tight nor loose.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin again with the extraction, and if the ligament is relaxed and the bone is dislocated, and similar things, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if it is necessary that the healing not be affected by the member, because it is too constricted, then soften it slightly and leave it thus for a few days, until the healing has improved, and then extract it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said comes to the illness, so do not cut off until after 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	or, in the case of wounds, then wrap his hands around his neck, and make his necks even, and prevent movement and injury, and let him sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and knows that this breaker is cured in 30 days or in 35, and perhaps in 20, according to the qualities and complexions of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the break in the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	And know that at the back of the hand and to us the two have few breaks, and there comes but a little pain many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the plant of the hand is broken or swollen, so that the patient cries out, and sits straight before him evenly;
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then place his hand on the tabletop, and spread out the minister's bones that are broken, and make them even the mirrors, as long as they are well joined;
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and put on plaster and staw, if abscesses do not come, then he puts a stake according to the quantity of the place;
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and be wrapped in a sheet of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the breaker is in the armpit around the belly of the plant, so make a spike of linen, and order the patient to strap it to his broken plant;
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then the stretching of a long rope, and its string is as great as the palm of the hand, and is stretched, as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if it is broken at the back, so that you put a steele on, and another desoze in the plant, so that the hands are open and straight, then tie it completely around the hand, and stop the blood between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	If it breaks on either of the two sides, let it be pulled out, if it is caught, so that it remains equal, as it should be;
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and stretch it with the palm, and if you see that it has a small straight stake to lift the break, and does not move;
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the break is like either of the two sides, that it is equal, and binds with the sound one who is after;
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you bind all together, so they do not move, or you put on a stake, as if it were caught;
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in the restoration and arrangement of the abscess, and protect him who comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken rib
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bones of the hip are often broken, and one can clearly see them when they move forward and backward.
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is good if we lay it on top of the fracture, and another above it.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies down, then each minister extends his bond to his side evenly;
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	is when the fracture is closed up.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	If the fracture is close to the root of the rib, then one of the ties is on the inside of the rib, and the other ties are on the outside of the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And if it is near the knee, then the bond is loose and the extension downward;
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then set the bone evenly with his two hands as it is in its natural position, and then put the plaster, and the bandages, so that there comes no blood.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a fever, let it rest, then return to your work and your treatment;
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The time is made in such a way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you wrap it up tightly on the wound with a hard cloth twice over or three times over, and leave aside the excess, then turn the leg around so that the heels come to the root of the naissance, and tie a long thread between the thigh and the leg, free the knee from the thread, and bring the head of the thread up.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	then turn around on the leg and on the thigh the bandage, then put on the wound some wooden splints, and put a splint on the bone of the leg;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	then employ the fire between the leg and the thigh of linen threads so as to make even the tying, then begin to tie in form III or IV on the wound;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and when you go up on the wound, and less the tying;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then take the two ends of the thread that you have tied between the leg and the thigh, and tie III splints that are above them, then go back to the end of the thread at the head, as far as you come from the foot;
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and restrain, so that it does not move from its place, then let it be, then if it comes to an abscess or floreat or other.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it happens, if it dislocates, and moves back in place, and comes again, as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are pieces of bone that he grabs, if it is necessary, let him do it;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if it cannot be done, if it is necessary to split the place, and pull hard;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And never break the pelvis in this way, as when the shoulder or arm is concerned;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	however, in the restoration made in this way, the patient does not become ill.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the chest is restored in a day, or less or more, according to the diversity of complexities.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the pit of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	that in the pit of the knee there is little fracture, but it bleeds many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, unless it is only a crack or a hole, and comes to all wounds, and not wounds, and this feels wrong.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is such that he places what is long at its two ends, as much as it can be assembled so that it can move;
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	and then set the plaster, and I put a round stick, if you need it, and hold it as necessary, then return all the dispositions that we have said in other breakers, like hot abscess and other similar things;
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then to each injury what he deserves, as long as he is healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	 knows that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called by right "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile";
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and all the breaks are like those of the arm, and so its restoration is also equal to that of the arm, and the work is complete. And if the two bones break together, then the leg returns on all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the bone is broken, then turn back.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, there is great pain, and it can be seen clearly;
et torne desoz.	and return sober.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then extend it, and make it equal, and bind the tendons equally;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	However, if it is broken, it is ugly, and there are many pieces, then the extension should be lighter and less severe;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and equal it according to your art.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have finished your work, take two long hair-braids and purple them the legs from the ankle to the foot on both sides, and let them be long enough for the feet;
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap them around the legs above and below, and bind them together in the middle, and at this bind the legs so that they do not hang to one side or the other, and so it is good;
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and there are no berets on the legs, and if necessary, put one leg forward to prevent movement, and properly make this wound in the fracture or where the injury is;
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move each leg every day to see if there is an abscess or another accident;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if the patient as long as he is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but at the foot there is a fracture in some cases, and in many cases it does not happen, but only is injured.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if there is a break in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones rub against each other, if the patient as long as he is healthy. If there is a break in the bones of the foot, put your foot on its own, so that where the bones are raised, then press them together until they come back into their places;
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	then put plaster on it and press it down, and make a small table of II flat boards, then tie it to the foot in front, and then that you have wrapped bandages around it, and other things that you need to do.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	When three or four days have passed, if the joint is still dislocated, for you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or not.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if there is one of the two broken, then restore them, as we have said about the bones in the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	and then on the two side cut a stone according to the length of the two, and one little more wide, and then set in the foot that I said, and draw out with care;
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are II or III, or more, cut on each of the two a stone according to its quantity, wrapped in a linen cloth, and draw out the foot that is sore with care;
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and let it be standing on the head of the foot that is sore so that it well shades it;
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And you must not forget the other things that I said to break with care, as soon as we have said;
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and cut each accident as it comes.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	the break of the bone between the knuckles
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the woman's bones are broken, if she is made to sit wide, then she leans on the back part and is held by behind;
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	and fill the bag with the cotton of the disease, and put it on as big as I am.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	Then bring the woman to stand, and tie her neck and back little by little, and then let the cotton go, until it comes to the entrance of nature, and returns the bones with the strap.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she goes to urinate, if the cotton comes out, and when she has finished, put it back, and do so for seven days or more.
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	then the break will be healed, and if you see anything, take a bladder of beef, and tie a cord to the peritoneum, and pour all of the bladder into nature.
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow into the cord until the bladder is inside:
la nature si revenra li brisure;	and nature will bring back the break;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then fill it with cotton and leave it like that for a few days, until it is well.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of the arm is broken, or that of the woman, so as to restore it as we have said in the leg bone;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these fractures are not hidden from him who puts his study and use into them, and hear my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fracture means many different things depending on the right path of restoration:
enten le donques.	Let us then begin.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the groin, when it is broken, take an goose's neck and insert it into the groin;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	Then wrap around the drapelets, and leave it for three days or more, and it will be healed without an hospital.
de brisure avec plaie	of break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for him who has broken with wound, great or small, such as the hip bone or shoulder or similar, to be healed now, so that the wounds which we have said bear witness to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, if the vitriol burn remains, if you have nothing else, then start to restore the broken one in the same hour or day, when the blisters come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the blisters come, if you leave the restoration until the next day, as long as the blisters are calm, and do not touch them on the third day or the fourth, because you would bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible on top of the skin, then you must put it out of joint lightly with your hands, in small extensions.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extensions do not appear to you to be equal to your hands, so that they can hold this instrument which is made of iron, which has seven or eight long fingers and whose breadth is determined by the quantity of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and for this reason it is necessary that he take three or four times the amount of the medicine according to what is needed in each healing of a broken bone.
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and be round and a little thick, so that it does not press on the member when it is wrapped up, and be larger in front and thicker in the middle: thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	is called "palatine", because it is necessary that the curved head be placed on the top of the prominent bone;
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and be stretched out once, until it recovers, and be even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle and the instrument cannot take the bone well, then you must chop off the head of the bone as long as the instrument has the power to do so.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, with the help of an appropriate tool, be it a chisel or a saw, at your power:
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then remove what is left in the bone with sharp and small cuts.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone has been set back in place, and the patient feels great pain after it, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	If it is in its place, then soak it in black vinegar, and properly so if it is in a solution.
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put anything on the wound except oil, or anything else that has oil, so that it does not cause inflammation and corruption.
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then administer the salves when you have set the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover all around it, according to the size of the wound, and take care that the wound is not pulled with the break;
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times have done this foolish trick, and have caused the patient to die or be corroded once;
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and let the extraction be softer and less painful than that of the other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident will not come, as we have said, and you feel pain at the site, then it is not good to put any salves on;
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but wrap tightly in linen, instead of wool, hard cloth, and tie it tight.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days to form a boil on the wound, then if you have put anything that you have put on all over, and you put a healing ointment, as a four-fold ointment and its likes.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at night, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs are arranged in such a way that the boil runs down轻松.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day it passes and he cannot join but runs together, knowing that there are little pieces of bone, so that you must cut the wound with a knife, and all these painful pieces that come out.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to light, or any other kind of corruption, then it is necessary that you cure it according to what he says in his chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken and opened up on the member, as the hip bone or shoulder bone, and other similar members, do not pull it out, for many times death comes from it, but leave it until it putsrefies.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	Maybe it will heal itself in about 20 or 30 days, then treat the wound if you can;
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you can't, let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	These bruise which come by the sudor
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We often come after the health of the broken one, especially when it is near a joint, and an ugly thing it is to see the shape of the member;
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and maybe can't do the natural work of the members.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Take care, then, if we free it:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if he administers harsh medicines, as aloes, incense, myrrh, and sulfur, or any of these things alone, or all together, and mixes them with wine infused with vinegar or with a lot of ink, or with honey;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and place them on the neck in steps, and hold them firmly, and do not let them slip out of your hands every day;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then dislodge it, and start another one, until the knots are cut;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or hold onto a piece of canvas that is well made;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the property of canvas is that it cuts off all the swellings from the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the knot is already hard like a stone, and it needs to be opened up, so as to cut off the surplus, leaving what appears to be the excess;
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	or hold onto a razor at all times until it is cut, and treat it until it is healed;
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the member which is weak after the jail
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the break in the bone has healed, and there are still weak and delicate limbs, this may happen because of:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	because one is because it was tied too tightly, and was not tied as tightly as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	Or why is there too much hair, and cannot come to the member's recovery?
ou por multitude d’arosement;	Or why is there a lot of inflammation?
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	Or why are there great movements, not in their hour?
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	Or why does the patient have little blood in his body, and is weak?
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body tender, until the blood increases in him;
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and give him baths, and give him joy and massage;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then put poultices on the member, so that the poultice attracts the great recovery, and is wet often with warm water, until the recovery runs to the member;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and return it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	two limbs twisted after sickness
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the member is twisted after the restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the form of the member is ugly, yet does not lose its natural work:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	If you don't believe the foolish people who say that a member should be broken altogether when it is new, and many foolish people have done this in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and these chapters are to blame, and great evil comes from them, and perhaps death;
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	However, if the joints and tortures are hot, or if herbs with a soothing action are cooked, as well as leaves of mallow, roots, and melilot, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and if the patch is made with a soothing substance, well done like a good squirt, and you take the musk of mallow, and confound it with linseed oil or seed oil, and make an ointment;
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	or if you take fig leaves, and grind them with hay of coleswort, and other medicines that soften the feeling of pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the neck moved by constantly and long-term friction with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And so let there be movement in each limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the curvature is strong and stiff, as in the case of a stone, it must be cut with a sharp knife lightly.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and put on leach-cloth and study in the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, if it is now brought back by gentle movement.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if one delays, if the veins swell, and by chance if one puts it back at the same level;
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	because it is not good that one moves it when it is swollen:
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	it often brings spasm and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	however, when it comes, make the patient well, then let it be, as long as the abscess is calm;
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then raise the member with hot water and oil, then move it lightly, and mend each member as the cure comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the antidotes for dislocations of the shoulders up to the tip of the finger.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	Note that the jaws may be dislocated upwards, and the dislocations of both are according to two manners:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	They are a little bone from their legs, and slightly softened.
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	They are completely dislocated, and hang down to the chest, and cause saliva to flow from the mouth so that they cannot hold it in, nor close their mouth, and wrap their tongue around with words.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocations are small, return them with many different positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	If it is complete and finished, then you must take her to the hospital right away, do not delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	And in such a way that the minister of the sick person ties the head, and pulls it with a little rope from one side of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, so that the dislocation is on two sides.
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other two hands are away, to make it even.
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And order the sick person that he soften his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And let him set his head to rest at equal intervals until it is back in place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if it is brought back, most certainly the two jaws are together, so they are raised with hot water and oil, until they are gently reset.
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	Do not tarry to bring me back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are brought back in even fashion, and the mouth of the sick person is well sealed with a mollifying balm, then put it on drapes moistened with oil and wax, and then lighten it gently by moving it.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the sick person sleep on their back, and have their heads between two pillows so that they do not move to the left or right, nor make any effort to turn over, but eat light food until the pains are relieved and the jaws are set.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then let him eat lightly, and do not bother to open the mouth for eating or drinking until the jaw is well set and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be reset to their places within an hour, and are not restored to their natural positions, then fever and heat set in customarily, and by chance there is an upset of the stomach, and by chance vomiting of clear fluid.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then know that it is a sign of recovery.
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many times dies those who have it, in nine days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	does not dislocate from inside the neck in the continuation of the windpipe and is dislocated at all times from the outside, and it can be felt clearly.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the cure is that the patient lies down on his back and extends his arms.
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the joint with your palm, and it will come back;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then put on the plaster and bandage, and holds it in place;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the shoulder that is next to the neck cannot be dislocated;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if not, and if it dislocates at all, then you put it back in place, as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put on the plaster and bandage, and holds it in place, and instructs the patient to rest as long as he is not well;
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and also the head of the shoulder, when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder can only be dislocated in three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	is dislocation due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is at the foot of the leg.
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and by chance it dislocates at the top, and there is pain.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and do not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and do not dislocate inside for the neck;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and many times it dislocates forward towards the axil, but at those who have dislocated their shoulder, because that is very serious, for that one will often be hospitalized;
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	at those who have enough dislocation, they are healed, and return to their normal state.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens that some men have a hit or a break, and the shoulder swells up with hot fever, and one believes that it has dislocated from this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	So then you must test it out, as long as you are certain of it;
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And there are two types of dislocation when it goes down towards the axil, and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them a manifest difference;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find at the head of the shoulder a pit, and remove the collarbone from the shoulder blade, as if it were an eye.
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor make any movements;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and if it is dislocated above, then it is not hidden, for you can see it clearly at the table;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this type of dislocation cannot be fixed unless it is new, or the patient has fallen ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the method is that the minister hold the patient's hand high up, then you remove the collarbone, and push the joint back into place with force.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the minister holds the hand high up, and then puts it back in place;
si venra hastanment.	so come to the hospital.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come as we have said, that the patient be bathed in hot water;
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and administer moistening and soothing preparations, as is done with an infusion of alfalfa and fenugreek and melilot in water, and let it be prepared;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then bring the patient to lie down on their back, and fasten a strap of equal length on one shoulder, neither too tight nor too loose, then put the foot of the affected leg on the strap, and gently pull up the head of the shoulder with your hand;
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and others minister to the patient's head so that he does not move around;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	now bring back the shoulder, and see if it comes back in this way:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and let a more experienced person be present who is larger than the patient;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and turn him away from the side, and fasten the shoulder of the patient, and lift it up so that the patient hangs;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And other ministers draw the arm of the sick man down towards his navel.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, with nothing heavy enough to hold it, the dislocation comes back again.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And this is how they do it in another way:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and stick a long piece of wood into the ground, so that the head is as far from the ground as a pistol, and not too thick or too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then it is placed under the sick person, but with a bed sheet over them, and the sick person is lying on the long wood;
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then their hand is extended down from the other side forming a shape, and the joint will come back to its place completely;
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	if it does not return to its place for all these things that we have said, then this is the treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	Take a piece of wood from two arms long and three fingers wide, which has the head at right angles to the end, in order for it to fit perfectly under the body, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	and then place it on top of the head with a long cloth, so that the patient is not injured, and then remove it from the patient's head;
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and extend your arms above the post, and place the shoulder on the post, and the arm at the top of the patient's head, then put the arm on a beam of a beam that is wide, and let it be extended down, and let the body hang from the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	the joint has now been realigned.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is ready in any way, so that you put an equal wool thread on the axle, then put the plaster prepared with powder from the mill, with incense and aloes of the egg, all over the shoulder and back, then remove the axle gradually, and tie the thread to the plaster, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let it rest thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary that he stretch a little, until the members are comfortable, because he will heal faster;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then stretch more after 5 or 7 days, and move him;
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if he is firm and has not become softened, then he is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has come out of its place due to moisture or any other cause, so that you make three piercings in it, as it is placed before or with the plaster of the piercings.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this, and he relaxes after 7 days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot raise his arms upstream, then you know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is cut or stretched or weakened;
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and knows that the joint never was set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	the dislocation which is above the hip, and the breasts, or behind, so is made by impact, and stretching of hands, and I administer another place;
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat as long as it is healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the recovery comes grit to the member, and late movement, then the patient uses it many times, until that grit is healed, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Knows that the joint at the neck is dislocated and returns to its place;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and has dislocated from all sides, and most of all in front and behind, and the dislocation is not returned to its place, for it can be seen well and felt well;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and is dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the ill shoulder with the sound one, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is decayed, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And it is necessary that you reset it in such a way as the legs come together, for if the legs come together, it would be painful to bring them back, if they were brought back;
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and may not be reset from all sides, most of all when it is behind;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	It is worse than other dislocations, and causes great pain, and sometimes it leads to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration is such that, when it is like this, so that you can bring it back, you extend its hand with your two hands;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And its arms spread out, and the hands face each other at the elbow joint from behind and in front, and push the joint into its socket, or at the root of the palm, until it regains its place;
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if he is dislocated in front, so he returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and proud of the root of the palm that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not return to its place, then administer strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and two ministers extend the arm, and turn it two ministers, so that he does not move at the extension;
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	Then turn the arm of each side, then you have wrapped a long and wide double cloth around it;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when you see the joint of the hand, if it is not oiled to soften the joint, then push the joint together, until it regains its place;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, put on plaster dry with ointment of sheep fat, and strain it, and hold the arm at the shoulder of the sick person, and leave it for a few days, then remove it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	and if the joint is stable in its place, then release the splint, and leave it;
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	and if you see that the joint is not well set, then begin again with plaster and the splint, and leave it in this way for a few days, until it is firmly set;
puis le deslie.	then remove it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	and if he feels pain after reducing the joint, and it moves, then bathe and gently massage it, and press until it is relieved;
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	or put on the joint a lamb's wool grease, then leave it for a day and a night, then the bone, and let it enter or bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when he sues, he rubs the joint well, then puts the young on top, and then goes in or bath;
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and so does it twice or three times until it is healthy;
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you want to see, put it at the end of a wet cooked bread and strain it out;
si revenra a sa disposition.	then return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and recovery is lighter than that of other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	However, it must be returned to its place carefully when it is dislocated, in the middle of the movement so that the bones do not hurt or come out with a hot poultice.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the way to do this is to put the bad hand on a table, and spread the fingers out wide, and look at them so that you make them all even, then put your palm on the appearance of the joint, and press it down until it comes back to life.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	However, it is necessary that you look to see if he is well placed.
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Then put the patient's back hand on a table for extension and retraction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, place the patient's palm down on the table and spread out their fingers.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, that is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	But if not, take the patient's arm and hold it so that the elbow joint faces upwards, and let it rest in this position while we continue.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you are unable to put him back in place after several days, then the joint will be twisted.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	And do not let the patient use his hands until his fingers are no longer swollen and he is able to grip things firmly again:
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	Then know that the nerve is cut, or an artery.
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	if there is no other way to extract it but by means of a delicate cautery tool, and perhaps nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put it on the pus as we have said, then extract it and leave it for 5 days, then take it off and leave it like this.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he can't move it well, and there is no fracture, if the hot water makes it moist, and rub it until it heals.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	No time do you dislocate the two fingers at each end, no time at the back of the palm or belly;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then put the two together and hold them close to the joints until they come back into place, then support the head of the two with your hand and turn it towards the part where they are joined;
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and leave it in that position for a day, and then make it even;
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and do not tie it up as we have said, and untie it by day, and let it move, and then tie it back up;
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this often, as long as it is tight, and in the same way if it has been dislocated at the bottom of the palm, and do so as you have done before until it is well;
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and in the same way when it has been dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the two fingers of the hand are not displaced at each end, nor on the back of the palm or belly; then they are bent, and shift the dislocation to the pouche until it returns
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the neck or collarbone is dislocated, or multiple dislocations occur, there will be no cure unless it is quickly treated, for death comes swiftly to the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the signs are that the excretions jump forth without will, nor can they be contained, and many times some member is softened, or both feet or both arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And many times the skin changes color in four parts;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	who changes color behind is called "gilbositez":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	the cure is that you reward it if the gilling has come from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	if there is no cure or recovery from all this.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling, or from blows, or from similar things, the ancient ways of curing with big words, or it does not at all bring great benefit;
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	But I have simplified it according to my intention, and I have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the gilling which comes from the back before, there is no beginning nor healing;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and I say that comes straight down the two sides, and can not be cured anyone but who properly comes at the back, as I said;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	is that the patient is lying on his face in an even position, and has a poultice applied to him so that he does not blister;
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then put a hot tong to the head on the ground shaped, and another one under the chest, and tie a bandage around the patient's body above the malady, and another one under the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and the two know the ropes, one to the head and the other to the chest between the two tongs;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and are firmly tied, the rope as we have said, and the mirrour places its hands on the spine shaped, until it revives.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not recover with this cure, then take a tumbler of three long arms, and cover the wall with it, and put the patient on one side, and pour the water from the tumbler over the spine covered with the wall, then place the middle of the tumbler on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and set the mirrore upon the other head of the table, and press it well, until it comes back to its place;
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and if you see, do this with your hand that twists.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And so that you set the two torches on the head of the sick person with a long pole, and between each torch, opposite and aside, a palm's width of space;
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and in each torch put a peg where the twist comes, and let the torch be firmly rooted in the ground so that it does not move;
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between each two torches put one torch turning, so that the line turns, and set two small torches of a palm' width long, to turn the twist;
